Women should be seen and not heard.

Homo’s are worshippers of the devil.

She stopped reading, instead trying to find a break in the circle that had trapped them. She needed to get Agatha out of there.

Rio felt an ice-cold hand on hers, felt sharp nails pressing into her wrist as the claws ripped her hand out of Agatha’s. She turned to see the old hag between her and her wife.

Before Rio had a chance to say anything, Evanora started:

“You evil little thing. You disgust me,” she spat above the chanting.

Her wife swallowed.

“What makes you think it is appropriate for you to walk around in such a public space holding hands with your slut. There are children present; do you not have any shame?”

Her wife, who had been frozen still, jumped into action then.

“Call my wife that again, and I’ll kill you.”

And when Agatha spoke, it wasn’t just a threat, it was a promise.

Evanora only laughed. “Then you’ll end up in prison just like I knew you always would. And don’t count on Daddy to bail you out like always, sweetheart. He always does what I tell him to.”

Agatha narrowed her eyes before she shifted her gaze to Rio.

“Let’s go, baby.” She held out her hand for Rio to take again before her mother smacked it. The sound ringing out over the chanting. Red started blossoming on her wife’s pale hand.

“Baby,” Evanora mimicked. “As if that is something you should ever call another woman.”

“Aggs,” Rio said, because why the fuck had she just been standing there letting her wife’s poor excuse of a mother speak to her like that? “You’re right, let’s go.”

Her wife nodded, and together, they began trying to leave the circle on opposite ends.

“Let her go,” Evanora ordered.

The protestors parted for Rio, and she made it out the other side. That went easier than she had expected. She walked around the throng to retrieve her wife…

Who hadn’t been let out.

Who was still trapped inside the crowd of protesters, face to face with her mother.

“No!” Rio yelled.

How had she been so stupid?

She surged forward only to be met with five beefy men blocking her path. They shoved her back, using their signs to push her further.

Now, was it a good idea for a trained FBI agent to display all of their abilities in the middle of Central Park on civilians? No. But they were the only thing stopping her from getting to her wife.

And Rio would do anything for her wife.

She shot forward again, using her speed as an element of surprise to yank one of the protest signs from one of the men’s paws for hands. He blinked at her before Rio started swinging. She flipped the sign so that the wooden plank it was stuck to was at the end and went for it.

It was a blur after that. Rio registered blows landing, wood splitting, blood dripping onto the sidewalk. But her mind told her, don’t stop until you get to Agatha.

When Rio came back to her body, the crowd had dispersed. The chanting had stopped, and the air was filled with groans and hard thuds of people running from the crazy woman whacking people with a ‘God saves all’ sign.

In her line of sight was her wife again. Her wife, whose mother’s hands were gripping onto either side of her head with a vice-like grip. Her wife, whose eyes were streaming with tears, as her mother whispered harshly against her face.

Rio was going to snap Evanora’s wrists.

She raised the now bloody, battered wooden plank of the protest sign.

“Get your hands off of your daughter before you no longer have any,” Rio grit out.

Evanora, the sick fuck that she was smirked. She put her hands up in surrender and backed away from Agatha.

“Remember,” Evanora sing songed. “You will always be nothing.”

Rio let the comment roll off her back because the only thing that mattered, the only thing that would ever matter, was her wife’s wellbeing.

“Mi amor,” she took a step forward as Agatha stepped back. Rio tried not to let how much that hurt her stop her. “¿Estás bien?” Are you okay?

Spanish because Evanora couldn’t understand it. Spanish because Agatha was the only one who could hear her that could. Spanish because no one existed in this moment but them.

“¿Nena?” Baby? Rio tried again.

Her wife’s eyes were glassy. Vacant. As if the lights were on but nobody was home.

Agatha took another step back, then another, until she turned.

She was running.

Rio dropped the sign in her hands as she watched her wife’s retreating form.

Evanora stepped into view, a smug fucking smile on her face. Rio’s fits curled into balls.

“When she leaves you,” Evanora told her, voice dripping with satisfaction. “Remember I told you so.”

Rio didn’t think before she brought her fist up and swung.

***

She could have anyone in the world, why on earth would she choose you?

Agatha’s feet carried her out of the park.

Soon enough that poor little slut will realise she’s bedded the devil.

Her tears blurred her vision. She couldn’t for the life of her see where she was going.

You drink and abuse substances because you can’t face yourself.

She knocked into a woman who started yelling at her. The words fell on deaf ears.

You will never be enough, Agatha. Not for me, not for your father, not for Wanda and certainly not for your son.

Her feet had carried her to a bar.

She shouldn’t. She fucking shouldn’t. She hadn’t turned to alcohol like this in years. She didn’t want to give the therapy sessions she’d been forced to attend after she’d shot the wrong person and blew up her life any credit, but they had helped.

She yanked the bar door open anyway.

I’m glad Wanda has Nicholas. You would’ve corrupted him. Turned him into pure evil just as you are.

Agatha turned off her location, got up onto one of the bar stools, and ordered three shots of vodka and a double vodka coke. She knocked back the shots as if it were as easy as breathing.

The bartender stared at her, his mouth agape.

She flipped him off before forcing him to pour her three more shots. She demanded a tray to carry her drinks and slipped into a booth at the back of the bar.

She gulped down another shot when her phone began to buzz.

Rio.

She’d forgotten she’d set her phone to let Rio’s phone calls come through regardless of whether she was on do not disturb or not. She watched the phone ring until it stopped, and when she swiped up to look at her notifications, she had five missed calls from her, three from Jen, and one from Alice.

She turned her phone off and knocked back another shot.

The acidic taste of the vodka burned her throat, and she welcomed it.

She needed every word her mother had said to her gone.

The five shots she’d done hit her all at once. The effects of the boose slamming into her head making her nauseous. A giggle climbed up her throat and left her mouth. She laughed as she thought about what happened. Seeing her mother, her mother slapping her, her mother telling her she was the devil in human form.

It was all so funny, wasn’t it? None of it was true.

It’s not true, Agatha reminded herself.

It’s not true, it’s not true, it is true, it’s not.

Her brain was getting confused. It wasn’t true.

But isn’t it?

She slammed back the last shot. Those manic cackles turning into soft sobs.

She pulled her glass of vodka and Coke towards her and took a sip, her tears slipping down her face and into the glass.

Agatha didn’t understand what was wrong with her. Her mother said shit like that to her all the time. Maybe it was because of yesterday, all those women going after Rio, because, like she’d realised, Rio could have anyone. And her mother seemed to know that, too.

And Nicky…was he better off with Wanda? Sure, she saw him almost every weekend, but her son didn’t really need her. She didn’t do the school runs, she didn’t make him breakfast every morning, she didn’t tuck him into bed at night. That was all, Wanda.

She’d been a pathetic excuse of a mother.

Was she her mother?

The thought made her stomach clench, and she dry heaved. Fortunately, nothing came out. When her breathing levelled out, she chugged the rest of her drink, liquid pouring down her chin as she drank.

She waved a bartender down and reordered her previous order.

***

Agatha didn’t know how long she’d spent at the bar, but by the time she’d been kicked out, the sun was setting, and it was raining.

She tried to turn on her phone but kept dropping it. She was so drunk she couldn’t get her body to operate normally. It had been a while since she’d drunk this heavily, and she’d almost forgotten what it was like to lose complete control over her body.

She cursed when she dropped her phone into a puddle. Cautiously, Agatha stooped down to retrieve it. There was no saving the thing; she tipped it forward, and water leaked from the speakers.

“Fuckingg greattt,” she slurred to herself.

You are your mother.

She winced when the thought slammed into her head.

It hadn’t worked. The alcohol.

When she used to do this, she’d drink until she couldn’t think straight, and the vitriolic thoughts disappeared. That hadn’t happened this time. The thoughts still came, and when they did, they were loud.

She stood up, swaying on the spot before righting herself. When she thought she was good enough to move, she started walking…or…stumbling towards her house. Wherever that was.

Agatha bumped into at least five people as she made her way down the street. They all grunted or screamed at her to watch where she was going. She acknowledged none of them. Somewhere along the way, she’d lost her phone. Dropped it and kept walking, not that she needed it; it didn’t work anyway.

Rain soaked her hair and drenched her clothes as she staggered her way down more streets. She was vaguely aware that her body was cold. She wasn’t because she couldn’t feel it, but her skin was riddled with goosebumps, and her lips began to tremble.

Nicky and Rio would be better off if you were dead.

That thought felt like someone had backhanded her.

She stopped dead in her tracks, hunched over, and threw up.

Was that true? She asked herself as she threw up. Because if it were, shouldn’t she just end it all now? Run out into the middle of the road and let a car slam into her.

It isn’t true. You are just drunk.

A pair of black leather shoes appeared next to her patch of sick.

“Are you okay, ma’am?” The pair of shoes asked.

“Do I look okay?” Agatha snapped.

The man stuttered. “I…er…n…no.”

“I’m glad we’ve cleared that up. You can fuck off now.” As soon as she’d finished her sentence, she hurled again, her sick splattering onto the man’s shoes.

The shoes retreated.

Agatha didn’t know how long she spent curled over vomiting with hard raindrops beating against her back, but when she was finally sure she was done being sick, the rain had cleared most of her vomit away.

She wiped her eyes and mouth with the back of her hand, and when she looked up, her heart skipped a beat.

Rio sprinted towards her and didn’t stop until she was holding her in her arms.

Agatha thought she was done crying, but when her wife squeezed her tightly, the floodgates opened again. She rested her chin atop Rio’s shoulder as the tears rolled down her face.

“You’re okay,” Rio soothed as she ran her fingers through Agatha’s wet hair. “I’ve got you. I have always got you.”

For the first time since she’d spoken to her mother, those thoughts, those vile, deceiving thoughts dissolved into nothing.

Agatha realised then, just like she had when Rio had kissed her for the first time, that no substance could ever do more for her than her wife did, would ever have an effect on her like her wife did.

Rio pulled back, wiping the rain and tears from her eyes. Her hands mirrored the placement of her mother’s hours earlier, except her nails weren’t digging into her skin. Rio’s hands were gentle, cradling her.

“You are not evil, Agatha,” Rio told her.

Even in the rain, even in her drunken state, she locked on to the brown eyes staring back at her. They were filled with such earnestness that Agatha found herself believing her.

Rio pressed their foreheads together as the rain continued to fall.

And because Agatha remembered how much her mother’s words had affected her wife the last time, she heard herself reply:

“And you aren’t nobody.”

Chapter 36

Chapter Notes

y'all...don't hate me...

See the end of the chapter for more notes

Time stopped as Rio held her wife in the rain. Agatha was the strongest person she knew, and yet right now she seemed so small, so heartbroken and destroyed by her mother’s abuse.

All Rio wanted to do was take care of her.

“Mi amor,” Rio said, pressing her thumbs into her cheeks to hold her head up. “Let’s go home, okay?”

Her wife nodded her head once.

Rio could tell she wasn’t quite with it. She smelt of alcohol and dingy bars.

She held Agatha to her side as she flagged down a cab. Once one arrived, she cautiously put Agatha in it and told the driver to drive slowly. Agatha had nuzzled into her side, her beautiful face covered by her head of wet hair.

The taxi pulled up to their house, Rio paid and helped her wife out of the car. She swayed as she placed both feet on the ground, her body slumping against the cab.

“Come on, baby,” Rio encouraged as she pulled Agatha’s body onto hers. “You have to let me hold you so the driver can leave.”

Agatha didn’t respond, just let Rio pull her off the cab. Once it had driven off, Rio started walking towards the house, her wife’s arm slung around her shoulder as Agatha tried to walk. This wasn’t working. They wouldn't be getting anywhere anytime soon.

“Would you be okay if I carried you?” Rio asked.

When Agatha looked at her, her pupils were blown so wide she looked like one of those cartoon babies. Rio’s heart broke as her wife nodded, her teeth digging into her bottom lip.

“You’re okay, baby,” Rio soothed as she picked her up bridal style and carried her towards their front door. “I’ve got you, okay?”

Rio made it up the steps before she put Agatha down again. She let them into the house, and her wife began to cry again.

“Hey,” Rio soothed. “What is it? Talk to me.” She tucked Agatha’s wet hair behind her ear.

She shook her head. “Please don’t make me,” Agatha’s voice was so small.

“Never,” Rio replied.

She wanted to know more than anything what her mother had said to her, but Rio also knew she had to be patient. Agatha hated talking far more than she did, and Rio would wait an eternity if that’s what it took.

“What do you need, sweetheart?” Rio asked. “Anything you want, anything in the world, and I’ll get it for you.”

Agatha looked at her with glassy eyes, taking her in. After a beat, she whispered, “I just need…I just need you.”

Rio’s lips curled into a small smile.

“And maybe a shower,” Agatha quipped.

Rio’s smile only grew. Even at her lowest, her wife was still finding ways to tease and make jokes.

“I can do that.”

Rio helped her wife undress and took care of her in the shower, washing the stench of alcohol out of her hair and off her body. Afterwards, she made Agatha avocado toast with eggs and tomatoes (one of the only things Rio knew how to make) and chamomile tea.

At first, her wife outright refused to touch any of it, but with soothing words and gentle kisses to her cheeks, Rio coaxed her into doing so. Agatha had eaten three-quarters of the toast before Rio allowed her to stop eating. But she did drink all the tea.

After that, Rio took her to bed. She rested her back against the headboard as Agatha curled into her, her head resting against her chest. She was trembling, whether that was from the fact she was still cold from being out in the rain or to suppress tears, Rio didn’t know.

She ran her fingers idly through her wife’s hair, scratching at her scalp to try and calm her as much as possible.

“If I fall asleep,” Agatha whispered, “Promise to still be here?”

Rio furrowed her eyebrows. Did her wife think she would leave her? Never again.

She pressed a kiss to the top of her head. “I’m not going anywhere, baby.”

The hand resting on her chest curled her shirt fabric into a small ball.

“I can hear your heartbeat,” Agatha told her. “It makes me feel safe. I don’t want you to get up, even if you need to pee or get water, if I fall asleep. I know that’s not fair of me, but I just-”

“Not going anywhere,” Rio repeated. “I’ll be right here. I promise.”

Agatha nodded.

They fell into silence, Rio’s fingers continued to play with her wife’s hair.

“When I needed Wanda,” Agatha spoke into the silence moments later. “She was never there. My mother would come over to our house, scream at me as she just did, and she would just…watch.”

Rio’s stomach dropped. Wanda, the person Agatha had loved so much, she chose to have a child with, watched as her mother verbally abused her? The hand in her wife’s hair tightened slightly as the anger started to rise.

“And once my mother was done,” Agatha continued. “She’d offer Wanda tea and cookies and leave me to go through my emotions alone.”

How?

The first thing Rio thought once Evanora had started spewing her bullshit was how to stop it, how to harm her in anyway possible. How could Wanda just stand there? The anger was manifesting into tears as they pricked her eyes.

“I never said anything because I loved her too much. But then there had been an issue with the law firm Wanda started; they had gotten into some money trouble, and she was going to lose everything. She never told me, but told my mother, and my mother paid to save it when I could’ve helped.”

So, Wanda was a fucking sellout.

“I couldn’t do it after that. She was wrapped around my mother’s finger, doing everything she asked. She became the daughter my mother never had.”

And in that moment, Rio hated Wanda.

“She never deserved you, mi amor,” Rio told her.

A breathy chuckle left Agatha’s mouth. “I know that now.”

“I’m not her,” Rio found herself saying, found herself needing to say. “Nothing in the world would make me betray you or Nicky like that.”

The fist clenching at her shirt tightened.

“Thank you.”

“You don’t have to thank me,” Rio replied, because she didn’t.

“Growing up,” Agatha started again.

“Wait,” Rio stopped her. She realised then that her wife was still drunk, and she probably should remind her of that fact before she started opening up. “You’re not sober yet, Aggs.”

She nodded. “I know, and it’s pathetic, but I don’t think I would be able to get this out properly if I were. Please just let me.”

“Just…are you sure? I don’t want you to regret this in the morning.”

Agatha nodded again. “My only regret is not telling you all of this sooner, for having to be fucking drunk to do so,” she laughed lightly.

Rio smiled. There would never be a more delightful sound in the world.

“Okay.”

Agatha inhaled a deep breath. “When I was growing up, I discovered I liked women pretty early on. To this day, I still don’t know how, but someone found out and it spread like wildfire. My mother, to no one's surprise, was not happy about it.”

Rio scratched lightly at her wife’s scalp.

“She had never treated me all that nicely before, but it just got worse. My father didn’t care, not really, about my sexuality, that is, until my mother told him it was cause for concern. So, she did everything in her power to try and ‘fix me,’ and my father paid for the best of the best.”

Rio hated this, hated that she couldn’t go back in time and change it all. When she’d come out to her Abuela, nothing changed. She’d told her she didn’t care, and she’d love her regardless of who Rio loved. She wished her wife could’ve had that.

“It didn’t work, obviously, so I just started lashing out. Sneaking out, sleeping with people I shouldn’t, drinking and drugs and all that shit because I just figured what did it matter? At the beginning of every summer, I would be shipped off to some troubled teens camp or conversion therapy, so I might as well make the most of my freedom.”

Agatha paused, snuggling deeper into Rio.

“Sex, drugs, and alcohol were the escape. But I realised today that it no longer is.”

“You’re healing, baby,” Rio told her. “And I am so proud of you.”

Her wife’s head tilted upwards, and Rio locked onto beautiful blue for the first time since they’d gotten into bed.

“It’s you,” Agatha told her.

Rio furrowed her eyebrows.

“You’re healing me.”

Rio blinked, and tears slipped down her face immediately. “Don’t give me too much credit.”

“It’s the truth,” Agatha replied firmly.

She put her head back down on Rio’s chest, and Rio pressed two kisses to her head.

Agatha didn’t speak again after that, and Rio couldn’t quite find the right words to say. She just held her wife and ran her fingers through her hair.

Rio didn’t know how long she did this before her wife fell asleep; she could tell by the soft snores that left her wife and by the way her mouth was slightly open.

She smiled. Agatha was truly perfect.

In the silence of it all, Rio found it was safe enough to whisper:

“I have an intense feeling of deep affection for you.” And she kissed the top of her wife’s head once.

***

This was the second time Agatha had woken up that morning. The first time, she needed to pee. It was around 6 AM. Because of her stirring, she had woken up Rio, too. Her wife also needed to use the bathroom, and Agatha realised she’d probably been holding it since last night after she’d asked her not to go anywhere.

They’d gone together. She didn’t know if it was how vulnerable she’d been last night or the hangover, but Agatha found herself being extremely clingy. She’d held Rio’s hand as she sat on the toilet and continued to hold on to it when it was Rio’s turn.

They’d climbed into bed again, neither of them falling back asleep quite yet. They just sat in a comfortable silence, clinging to each other.

About an hour passed before Rio said she wanted to make breakfast, and if it would be alright for her to leave to do so. Agatha had nodded, and her wife had left. She meant to follow her, but she’d ended up falling asleep again.

Two hours later, Agatha was blinking awake, and Rio hadn’t returned.

She groaned as she pulled herself out of bed. Her head was throbbing, and her throat was dry. She brushed her teeth and washed her face before heading to the kitchen.

What day even was it?

Her wife greeted her with a smile when she entered the room.

“Good morning.”

“Morning,” Agatha yawned.

She stopped when she took in Rio’s appearance. She was wearing a green apron that was covered in what looked like cinnamon. Cream was smeared across her face and elbows and the kitchen looked like a bomb had gone off.

It was possible her wife made an even bigger mess than Nicky.

“What are you-”

“How are you feeling?” Rio cut her off.

“Better.”

And she meant it. Minus the hangover, she felt as if a weight had been lifted off her shoulders. She’d finally been able to tell Rio everything. Agatha wasn’t proud that she’d needed alcohol to do so, but she didn’t trust herself not to chicken out if she attempted to do it sober.

She loved Rio, but talking about her feelings was something she still found insanely difficult. But she was working on it.

“You still haven’t answered my question, though. What are you-”

Her wife tugged her in by the waist and cut her sentence off with a long, deep kiss.

She pulled away with a smile. “You’re trying to distract me…why?”

Rio feigned obviousness. “Am I?”

“Rio,” Agatha warned.

“Do you want bagels?” Rio asked, changing the subject yet again. “Because I still haven’t tried those Jo’s bagels you and Jen won’t stop raving about, and you always tell me they're the best hangover cure.”

“I thought you were going to make breakfast?”

Rio waggled a finger at her. “That was two hours ago…plus I burnt it all.”

Agatha furrowed her eyebrows. “Then what’s all-”

“So, bagels?” Her wife cut her off again

Agatha was getting more frustrated by the minute.

“Yes,” Agatha replied with gritted teeth. “Bagels sound nice.” As much as Rio was pissing her off, she really did want those breakfast bagels.

“Great! Can you go get them?”

Agatha jerked her head back. “But you were the one who-”

“I know, but I need to go shower and clean up the kitchen, baby. I mean, look at me, I can’t go out looking like this.”

“I can help, and then we can go together.”

Rio shook her head. “Nope, nope. You gotta go now, otherwise they’ll run out of the breakfast bagels. Isn’t that what you and Jen always tell me? They're always gone by 10:30?”

Unfortunately, her wife was right, and Jo’s bagels didn’t do Uber Eats. What food establishment didn’t do fucking Uber Eats?

Agatha narrowed her eyes. “Rio Vidal if you don’t tell me what the fuck is going on right now, I swear to-”

“Fine, fine,” Rio replied. “I promise I’ll tell you…when you get back.”

Agatha opened her mouth to argue when Rio tilted her head and stared at her with a pointed look.

She was the only person in the world who could get Agatha to do as she asked.

“Fine,” Agatha huffed.

“Good girl,” Rio told her before giving her a quick kiss.

Agatha rolled her eyes before turning to leave.

“I miss you already!” Rio called after her.

She flipped her off.

***

Agatha was making her way back to the house with a large paper food bag and two flat whites in hand.

She was fuming, to say the least.

Why was Rio being so secretive? And why hadn’t she wanted to come with her? And why was their kitchen a mess?

She rounded the corner, and their house came into view.

I have an intense feeling of deep affection for you.

What was that? The thought made Agatha blink. That was Rio’s voice in her head. Had she dreamed that?

Her mind cast back to last night, to when she was slipping into sleep and Rio had whispered…

Agatha stopped abruptly.

That was the textbook definition of love. Her wife had told her she loved her without actually saying she loved her.

What the fuck?

Why had Rio said that to her when she thought she was asleep? Could her wife not say it to her face? Now Agatha was even more pissed.

She stormed up to their house and hurriedly opened their front door to confront her wife.

She stopped short for the second time in two minutes.

Hanging in their hallway was a banner.

Happy Birthday!

In purple and gold.

Agatha had completely forgotten what day it was, yesterday’s events ensuring it. She smiled.

“Sneaky bitch,” she muttered to herself.

She walked into the living room and found it decorated with more banners, purple, white and gold balloons were scattered about the place and on their table was a handful of presents.

Agatha’s smile only grew.

“You’re not slick for this by the way!” Agatha called as she made her way to the kitchen.

Rio wasn’t there.

Agatha rolled her eyes playfully; her wife was going to make her find her. She placed the food and drinks down on the now clean island. She began to make her way to the elevator when Rio’s phone buzzed in her back pocket. Rio’s phone because she still didn’t have one from when she’d lost it yesterday. Her wife had told her to take hers and call her on the landline if she needed anything.

She took it out of her pocket and clicked it on.

Unknown number: Happy birthday, Agatha.

She furrowed her eyebrows. Who was-

Her eyes caught sight of drops of crimson just ahead. Blood. And a shattered glass.

No.

“Rio!” Agatha screamed.

She ran out of the kitchen and found there were more drops of blood further down the hall passed the elevator. She followed the trail until it stopped just short of their back door that had been left slightly ajar.

No.

Agatha shook her head furiously. No. No. No.

She flew to the elevator and pressed the button frantically. When it arrived, she got in and headed straight for the basement. She called out Rio’s name and checked every room. She wasn’t there.

Agatha returned to the elevator and took it up to their bedrooms. She yelled Rio’s name as she pushed open every door until she made it to their rooftop garden.

There was still no sign of her wife.

“Rio!” Agatha called desperately as she stepped out of the elevator and made her way back to the living room.

Agatha searched the house five times before she ended up back in the kitchen. She was sweating, panting like crazy, and tears were beginning to prick her eyes.

She shook her head as tears slipped down her face. The conclusion was clear.

Rio’s phone buzzing again only confirmed what she already knew.

Unknown number: Good luck finding her.

Agatha hunched over and threw up.

Chapter End Notes

Chapter 37

Chapter Notes

y'all the plot had to plot I'M SORRY, how else would you be entertained???

See the end of the chapter for more notes

Rio blinked awake, finding she couldn’t see a thing. Wherever she was, was void of light.

She had a brief moment of peace before pain started spreading through her brain. She winced as it only got worse. The left side of her forehead felt damp, sticky with something she knew could only be blood. She went to touch it and found her hands had been bound. The chains jangled as she moved, doing nothing for her headache.

What the hell had happened?

The last thing she remembered was getting out of the shower and changing as fast as she could to make it back in time to prepare the kitchen for her wife’s return.

Her wife.

“Agatha!” Rio called even though she knew it was probably futile. “Agatha?” Rio called again, except this time it was barely a whisper.

She knew the beautiful voice and the woman who owned it would not reply.

How had she let this happen? How had she let someone take her? Rio was good at her job, she could sniff out an attack from a mile away, so why not this? Why hadn’t she seen signs in her own home?

There was no point in dwelling on it. What’s done was done. The only thing Rio had control of now was getting out. And she would, no matter what it took.

She twisted her hands in her cuffs to see how much room she had. None. They’d been fastened perfectly, almost as if they’d been designed for her. Rio leaned forward and picked up the chain in her hands, yanked once, twice. No give.

Pain shot through her again, but this time it came from her right arm. She noticed then that it felt weaker than the other, sensitive even. As if someone had stuck a needle in it. She realised she was probably right.

Rio huffed, her eyes darting about the place to see if she could make out anything amongst the darkness. She couldn’t. Maybe she should try standing, see how far she could walk. She went to do just that only to find her feet had been chained to the ground as well.

She crashed back down to earth with a yelp, her chains rattling as they hit the floor, the ache in her head spiking.

“For fucksake,” Rio muttered.

What sounded like bolts unlocking rang out. The noise from the chains must’ve notified her attackers. Good. Rio was ready to kill someone.

What felt like centuries later, the door unlocked, and a thin stream of light shot down the room as the door creaked open. Rio heard a man and woman speaking in what sounded like Spanish, what they were saying unclear.

She craned her neck to try and see who spoke until the man came into view, blocking the light and plunging her into darkness once more. He stood and stared at her for a long moment, and Rio was desperate to see who he was.

CLICK!

Light. Rio squinted, blinking rapidly to get her eyes to adjust. She made out the figure of the man approaching her before he crouched just before her. She forced her eyes to remain open as she took him in. He kind of looked like someone she…

Daniel Gomez.

The man from the Miss America shoot-out, the man her wife was convinced was trying to shoot at her instead of their mission subject, Kalani-Rose.

Rio jerked her head back. “You?” She scoffed. “What the fuck?”

Daniel furrowed his eyebrows as if he couldn’t believe that was all Rio had to say. “I…” he started.

She stared at him, her expression unimpressed.

This was fucking ridiculous. Her kidnapper was just some random. Not a long forgotten enemy or someone out to seek revenge. Just a man she’d never even spoken to or seen before until he was blasted all over the news.

“What the fuck do you want?” Rio asked because now she was fuming. It was her wife’s birthday, and this man (like most men do) was ruining everything.

He blinked at her.

“Well?!” Rio yelled.

She was clearly throwing him off. He probably expected to go in there and be the big bad attacker, and that Rio would cower and shake in her bones at the mere sight of him. The thought that she’d dismantled this dream made her feel warm and fuzzy.

Daniel blinked a few more times before he steeled himself. His face twisted into a somewhat serious expression. He reached his olive hand up to touch Rio. On instinct, she jerked her head back. His hand kept advancing until Rio’s head was pressed against the wall.

With nowhere else to go, his hand finally made contact with her skin, brushing at her cheek, tucking her hair behind her. She felt sick; the only person who could touch Rio like that was Agatha. When Daniel went to brush her other cheek, Rio lunged forward to bite him. His finger just avoided being bitten off.

He scrambled backwards as if she were a wild animal. Rio flashed him a toothy grin.

“Try that again and I will bite your hand off.”

Daniel narrowed his eyes before surging forward and shoving a needle in her arm.

Fuck, fuck, fuck. No! Fight it!

She couldn’t, she felt her consciousness slipping away from her by the second.

Daniel slid behind her, putting his back against the wall and cradling Rio in his arms. She couldn’t even yell at him to get off her, threaten him, fight him. Tears slipped down Rio’s face as Daniel stroked her hair and shushed her quietly. She felt him press a kiss to her cheek, and she wanted to scream.

As Rio’s eyes began to flutter shut, only one thought came to mind:

I love you, Agatha.

***

I miss you already.

That was the last thing Rio had said to her; the last thing Rio might ever say to her. And what had Agatha said? Nothing. Too irritated to tell her the same. Too caught up in being mad about something so fucking stupid she hadn’t given her wife any last words to cling on to, like Rio had her.

I miss you already.

Not nearly as much as me. Agatha should’ve said. Because that’s what she always said.

But not this time. Not the one time Rio actually needed to hear it.

After Agatha finished throwing up, the doorbell rang. She grabbed one of the hidden guns in the kitchen and made her way to the door, prepared to shoot at anyone who dared to attack her as heartbroken as she was.

It was Jen and Alice coming over to celebrate her birthday.

She let them in, told them everything, and cried in her best friends arms.

Alice stepped away to report Rio’s kidnapping to the FBI, and Jen suggested they go out and try to track her phone's location. This only made Agatha sob more because she’d lost her fucking phone. She’d lost her phone, and Rio had given her hers.

Why did she have to do that? Get drunk yesterday? She didn’t even need the alcohol, it hadn’t worked. Rio was the only thing that worked. And now Agatha might’ve lost her.

She should’ve woken up earlier and gotten the bagels earlier so she wouldn’t have missed the attack, she should’ve forced Rio to come with her, she should’ve walked home faster, she should’ve ordered less, and then she would have made it back sooner.

“Hey,” Jen said softly, dragging her out of her thoughts. “Come on, I’m driving us to MO.”

Agatha nodded.

As she sat in the back of Jen and Alice’s car, Agatha kept clicking Rio’s phone on and off. She had her lock screen set to a photo shuffle so that every time you unlocked it, the picture would change. When Agatha unlocked it next, it was a photo of her and Rio in Portofino for her birthday. They both had pasta coming out of their mouths as they flipped off Alice, who had taken the photo from the bar.

The next photo came up. It was only of Agatha. She’d never seen this photo before. She was in their cinema room, head resting on her propped-up hand as she stared at whatever film she was watching, wrapped up in blankets.

The phone switched off again, and Agatha clicked it on once more. This photo was another one of her and Rio. Jen had taken this one. They’d all decided to go on a walk around Central Park. Alice and Jen had been late. Agatha and Rio were waiting on one of the benches for them. They were leaning into each other; Rio was tucking hair behind Agatha’s ear, and Agatha looked so in love.

Because she was…is.

Next, it was Rio, Nicky and Agatha. Rio had taken it in their bathroom mirror as they were brushing their teeth one morning. Nicky had toothpaste coming down his mouth, and Rio was laughing, Agatha smiling.

Nicky.

“Jen! Jen, give me your phone.”

Jen did so without question. “What’s up? Is everything okay?”

No. Everything was not okay.

She searched through Jen’s contacts until she found ‘Agatha’s bitch ass ex’ and dialled.

The call went to voicemail.

No.

Agatha dialled again.

***

They’d moved her.

Rio was no longer chained to a wall; she was in a chair, handcuffed (obviously), sitting at a table. The room was small…like a shoe box, white…clinically white. It reminded her of the room at main operations she’d been in the day she’d joined The Smith’s Programme; the day she married Agatha.

Her arm was twice as sore now after the second injection. Rio realised she needed to play her cards right if she wanted any chance at escaping. It seemed as if the moment Rio did something Daniel didn’t like, he’d sedate her. She couldn’t do a thing if she were unconscious.

The door to her left opened, and Daniel stepped inside, a smile on his face.

When Rio was free from her chains, she was going to kill him.

He sat down on the chair opposite her, his smile unwavering. “You could’ve been everything, you know?”

Rio just glared at him. She didn’t have time for the cryptic talk. She wanted him to say what he wanted and get this over with.

“We knew, they knew, and yet they kept you away from us. But here you are anyway.” Daniel grinned. “The princess finally home to her castle. Pity you don’t get to stay.”

Rio didn’t say anything.

“Oh, come on,” Daniel leaned forward. “You’re not even the slightest bit curious as to what I’m talking about?”

“No.”

Quite frankly, Rio didn’t give a single fuck. She just wanted to get home to her wife.

“Hm. I’m gonna tell you anyway.”

Rio rolled her eyes.

“A long time ago…well…just over thirty-three years ago now, actually. A man and a woman had a daughter. Any guesses on who that might be?”

Again, Rio deadpanned.

“Well, it just so happens to be the beautiful woman in front of me.”

Rio wanted to throw up.

“Anyway, this man was very important to this group of people, he was a king. And his daughter…she was supposed to take over after his reign. But he hid her from the people, their princess, their predecessor.” Daniel paused before he said, “So naturally…we killed his wife.”

Rio’s eyebrows furrowed. Then it hit her.

Her mother.

She never actually knew how her mother died. Her Abuela had told her she was sick, and the sickness took her. Rio never questioned it as she couldn’t remember much about her mother anyway.

“You killed her?” Rio asked, her voice quiet but stern.

Daniel smiled. “Anyway, the king left his people for good after that, and the princess was lost to the world. We got whiffs of clues as to where she was here and there, but nothing solid. Until we got a call, someone knew who you were and where we could find you. And here we are.”

“Whose we?” Rio shot back. “And who told you?”

Daniel tutted. “All in good time, princess.”

Rio fucking hated that pet name.

Her mind was racing. This didn’t make any sense. Her father was king, king of what? Rio was pretty sure her father had worked at a repair shop fixing cars. There was no king’s needed in garages. And who the fuck was we and why did they want to kill her? It wasn’t her fault she didn’t know her family legacy.

Daniel rolled up his shirt sleeves, and Rio caught sight of the start of a tattoo. It appeared to be a long, blacked-out line.

The door knob twisting caught Rio’s attention. The door opened slowly to reveal a woman behind it.

Huh?

Marina Blue. The Serpiente gang leader.

Wasn’t she on trial? Wasn’t she behind bars? How? What?

She smiled, her perfect teeth on display. She wore a fitted black suit with no shirt underneath, her dark hair that reached just past her shoulders was in loose waves, her olive skin still managed to glow regardless of the weird lighting, and her dark eyes gleamed with fascination as she took Rio in. She was holding a file under her armpit.

“A Vidal in the flesh. Never thought I’d see the day.” Marina stepped into the room. “Get out, Daniel.”

“But I’m not done with her yet.”

“I don’t remember asking. Get up and get out.”

He rolled his eyes before doing as he was told.

Marina took his place opposite Rio.

“First things first. You will not try to escape; you will not go with Agatha if she finds us, and you will not give her or Alice or Jennifer any clues as to your whereabouts if we let you out in the open.”

Rio forced herself not to furrow her eyebrows. How the hell did she know her wife and friends' names? She’d let them roll off her tongue so effortlessly. And out in the open? They wouldn’t be so stupid as to let Rio out, would they? She hoped they would be smart enough to know the second she had the chance, she’d take it.

“And,” Marina continued. “I think you might want to see these before you get any ideas.”

She opened the file and spread out the contents within on the table.

Rio’s heart dropped.

Chapter End Notes

Chapter 38

Chapter Notes

you might need a box of tissues for this one...

See the end of the chapter for more notes

Agatha still hadn’t heard from Wanda.

She’d called her next to thirty times by now and had gotten nothing. Agatha had thrown up again. The thought that Nicky could be gone too threatened to kill her, would kill her, if Nicky and Rio didn’t come out of this alive.

They’d driven to Wanda’s apartment and found nothing. It appeared everything had been left undisturbed (Agatha knew where Wanda hid the spare key and had let them inside), but it didn’t explain their absence.

Now in main operations, a team of intelligence agents, led by Agent Calderu, were searching for Rio. After giving a detailed report on what had happened, Lilia had told Agatha to sit tight until they found something. She couldn’t. Instead, she logged into her home's security cameras to watch the footage with Jen and Alice, only to find the footage had been cut.

Agatha almost threw something.

She didn’t know what to do. She felt so helpless, and guilt was clawing at her insides because if she’d just been smarter, faster, more alert, then she could’ve stopped this. Rio would be safe and sound in her arms and not gone or potentially dead.

She ran out of the room to throw up again.

Many gruelling hours passed without any good news, or news at all for that matter. The sun had set, and Agatha still hadn’t heard from Wanda. She was starting to get so desperate that she was contemplating calling her mother.

Agatha was no longer in the room with the intelligence agents or Jen and Alice. The room was suffocating, trapping her within like a mouse in a shoe box. Instead, she walked aimlessly around MO as her mind spun out of control.

She missed Rio so much she felt like she couldn’t breathe.

How was she going to continue to live if Rio and Nicky were found dead? She’d been thinking about it, and the thought was so horrifying it physically stabbed her in the heart every time it crossed her mind.

Agatha was nothing without either of them.

She was walking to the toilet to throw up again when she locked eyes with dark brown. Not her dark browns but ones she recognised.

“It’s you,” the little girl said, smiling with her big brown eyes.

It was the brave girl from the Zip and Zazzle mission many months ago. The mission where the children had been forced to be slaves and housed in cages. Hihi had notified them when the children had been saved but Agatha never thought she’d see the girl again.

“Hello,” Agatha got out. Her voice was raw and scratchy from all the vomiting. “How are you?”

“I’m free,” the little girl laughed, her dimples deepening.

She looked even younger now in the bright lights of the FBI headquarters. But her cheeks were full, she wasn’t as thin, and her eyes had a sparkle in them instead of being empty and hollow.

“I’m glad,” Agatha smiled.

The girl nodded. “I have to come here for therapy every week, but I like to stay longer. I think I want to be an agent, help people…or try to. Like you.”

Agatha could’ve cried. Instead, she inhaled and kept them at bay. “I think you’d be a great one.”

“Thank you,” the girl replied. “I’m Nicole, by the way. What’s your name?”

Nicole. Kind of like Nicky.

“I’m Agatha, nice to meet you,” Agatha offered her hand to shake.

Nicole stared at it for a long moment before she ignored it completely and stepped towards Agatha, wrapping her small arms around her stomach.

Agatha was going to lose it again; she felt the tears prick her eyes immediately. She bit her lip to fight them off as she wrapped her arms around Nicole.

“Thank you again,” Nicole mumbled into her chest. “Seeing you gave me hope again. It reminded me to keep fighting.”

Agatha wanted to ask her how because she hadn’t done anything. She couldn’t even save Nicole when she’d wanted to. She had to leave her behind.

“You’re welcome.” Agatha crocked.

Nicole stepped back with a small smile. “You also made me want to learn how to fight. When you and your partner started battling it out, amongst all the fear, I couldn’t help but thinking how cool it looked.”

Somehow, Agatha found it in her to laugh.

“Are you two friends again? That argument was bad.”

Agatha chuckled. “She’s actually my wife,” Agatha replied. “And yes, we’re fine now.”

They were not fine, far from it.

Nicole lit up at the word wife. “That’s so cool! She’s your wife and your partner? I’m definitely joining the FBI now.”

Agatha smiled. “I’ll be looking out for you then, Agent Nicole.”

The girl's glee only grew. “See you around, Agent Agatha.”

“See you,” Agatha replied as Nicole walked away.

Agatha let out a deep sigh. That brief break from reality was much needed, but when reality settled in again, it was a punch to the gut. She made a beeline for the toilet.

***

It was 11:30 PM when Nicky and Wanda burst through the doors of MO. Nicky ran straight towards her, a smile on his face as he launched himself into her arms.

Wanda had finally called her back. She had taken Nicky to the Hamptons to visit his grandpa and hadn’t been on her phone all day. Agatha would scream at her for it later, right now, all she cared about was that Nicky was safe.

She’d told Wanda briefly what had happened and told her to come straight to MO when they returned to the city.

“Happy birthday, mama!” Nicky squealed.

Oh, right. It was still her birthday.

“Thank you, baby,” Agatha replied as she squeezed him tightly.

She could breathe slightly easier now that she had Nicky, and she could protect him. It was one less problem to worry about on her list of many.

“Why are we at your work, and where’s mami?”

The question was so innocent, so sincere.

Where’s mami?

She didn’t know.

Agatha told Wanda not to tell Nicky that Rio was missing. What would be the point? It would only upset him. Agatha didn’t trust herself to be strong for him, to not break down and cry when explaining to him.

She inhaled sharply as Nicky pulled back, his brown eyes locking onto her expectantly as he waited for an answer.

“She’s not here right now, Nicky,” Agatha forced a smile.

His eyebrows furrowed. “Why not? I wanna see her.”

Me too. “She’ll be back soon. She had to go away for a bit.”

Nicky frowned. “She left us behind?”

“She didn’t want to,” Agatha replied in barely a whisper.

“But-”

“Hey, Nicky,” Jen’s voice cut in. “My god, you’ve gotten so big!”

He giggled, and thankfully, the frown vanished. “Thank you, Auntie Jen.”

“This is my wife, Alice,” Jen introduced.

“Nice to meet you, Nicky,” Alice smiled.

“You too.”

Her best friend and her wife spent the next thirty minutes entertaining Nicky as the FBI sorted out a safehouse for the five of them.

***

Three days.

Three days with no news on Rio. She hadn’t been picked up on any CCTV cameras, and there hadn’t been any sightings of her. It was almost as if she’d vanished off the face of the planet.

Agatha hadn’t been eating…or sleeping for that fact. She spent her days with the intelligence team, walking about MO or spending time with Nicky. He grounded her, gave her hope because Nicky had returned to her unharmed. Which meant Rio could return to her too.

She was in the bathroom washing her hands when Rio’s phone buzzed. She grabbed it from her back pocket immediately and clicked it on.

Unknown number: You want your wife? Come get her.

The next message was a location. A warehouse upstate.

Unknown number: Come alone and don’t tell anyone, or she’ll be dead before you even step foot in the building.

It was all Agatha needed. She didn’t stop to think about whether this was a trap, or if she should tell someone and get back up. This wasn’t smart, and she knew it, but she didn’t care. Love made her stupid, and although Agatha prided herself on being anything but, this was Rio.

She grabbed her gun and her car keys and made her way upstate.

***

The warehouse was old and abandoned.

It was tucked away in the middle of nowhere, and there was no indication that anyone was in it at all. That was a major red flag and only encouraged Agatha’s suspicion that this may be a trap.
She went inside anyway.

The large space was cold compared to outside. A chill ran down Agatha’s spine as she took in the place littered with stacks of wooden planks that reached the ceiling. She pulled out her gun and ventured further into the warehouse.

Agatha went down the rows of wood that split the place up into long corridors. She went gun first as she stepped into each row, her eyes scanning for something, anything that might give away why she had been asked to come here.

She was nearing the last couple of rows when Agatha started to lose hope. Either she was about to be trapped herself, or someone was getting off on messing with her. She didn’t have time for this, not when she could be out looking for Rio, not when Rio was missing, not when Rio was right in front of her…

Her back was turned, but Agatha would recognise that head of dark shoulder-length hair anywhere.

“Baby?” Agatha asked, her voice hesitant even though she knew it was her.

She watched Rio’s body go rigid, watched her turn slowly, watched her face twist in horror.

Agatha was taken aback by Rio’s expression, but shoved the thought away because who cared right? Rio was in front of her, and she seemed unharmed, apart from her right hand, which had a white bandage wrapped around it.

“You’re okay!” Agatha exclaimed. When she stepped towards Rio to hug her, her wife took a step back.

She tried to ignore how much that hurt.

“What are you doing here?” Rio’s voice trembled.

Agatha furrowed her eyebrows. When she pictured them reuniting, it had not gone like this.

“I-” she started, then stopped because she genuinely didn’t know what to say. Why was Rio acting like this?

“You need to leave,” Rio told her.

Agatha blinked, words getting lost on her until she realised the reply was obvious. “Not without you.”

Rio shook her head.

“What’s going on?” Agatha took another step forward as Rio stepped back. “Why are you acting like this? You're safe now, I’ll protect you.”

Rio shook her head again. “No,” she whispered. “Please…please, you need to go.”

Agatha was getting pissed off now. Did her wife not trust her to protect her? Why couldn’t Rio see that now they were together again, they were back to being a team? A team that jumped out of planes and blew up buildings. A dead shot and one of the best agents in the field. A team that knew what the other was going to do without even a glance passing between them.

Like Agatha had said, she’d met her match, and she felt sorry for the world that it’d probably have to pay for it.

Today was no different. She and Rio were getting out of her, and after that, they would hunt down every last person that had anything to do with Rio’s kidnapping. Together.

“I’m not leaving you,” Agatha shot back. “Not unless someone killed me, and even in death I wouldn’t. I’d haunt you in my ghost form.” Agatha had to joke, had to try and make Rio laugh because for the past three days they’d both been in hell.

But Rio didn't laugh, didn’t even smile.

“If you won’t leave, then I will.”

Rio turned to leave, and Agatha grabbed at her arm. She spun Rio around, and Agatha had to block the fist that was aimed at her face.

She jerked her head back, betrayal sinking into her stomach because why had Rio done that?

Her wife was glaring at her as she tried to yank the arm Agatha was still gripping free.

“Let go of me!”

“Tell me what’s going on? Who took you? Why don’t you want to come with me?”

Rio was getting more frustrated with every question. She brought down her free hand onto Agatha’s arm, hitting it like a knife slicing through vegetables. Agatha snatched her arm back with a yelp as pain spread through it.

“Rio, what the hell?!”

Her wife was turning to leave again, and Agatha grabbed her wrist once more.

Yet again, Rio tried to punch her, and Agatha had to block it. She twisted her wrist sharply and freed herself before shoving Agatha back roughly.

Agatha stared at her, her chest rising and falling, her heartbeat thumping wildly against her ribcage. “Why are you doing this? Talk to me.”

“I’m leaving,” Rio replied matter-of-factly.

Again, Agatha wouldn’t let her. Why did Rio think she could just walk away from this? From them? And Agatha would just let her?

She grabbed at Rio’s arm again, twisted her around and crashed their lips together. She hoped the kiss said: I’m here, I’m not leaving you, I love you.

Rio pushed her back. The expression on her face, which was pure anger mere moments ago, was pained. Agatha could see the tears collecting in her eyes.

“Don’t do that,” Rio whispered.

“Why not?” When Agatha stepped towards her this time, her wife didn’t step back. “Why not, sweetheart?” She asked softly.

She pulled Rio into her arms and hugged her. Agatha hadn’t realised it until Rio gripped her back, but her body had felt like lead. Having Rio pressed against her made her feel light as air. She could breathe again, function like a human being again.

“You’re never going to let me go, are you?” Rio spoke moments later from where her chin was resting on Agatha’s shoulder.

“Never,” Agatha replied as she cradled Rio’s head. “Whatever is going on with you, you’re going to tell me and we’re going to deal with it together. Like always.”

Rio let out a noise that seemed to be a cross between a sob and a frustrated huff.

Agatha only gripped her tighter (if that were even possible). Whatever it was that Rio’s attackers had on her must be bad for her to be acting like this. She let her body sink further into her wife’s hold, relaxing until…

Wet?

Agatha felt something trickling down her leg, she furrowed her eyebrows until a stinging started up in said leg.

When Rio stepped back, Agatha looked down to find a knife buried in her right thigh. She snapped her head up and looked at Rio in horror.

Her wife had stabbed her.

“I don’t…I don’t understand,” Agatha got out.

Rio was wearing her unsettling mask of detachment. Agatha hadn’t seen it in months.

“You can’t chase me down if you can’t run,” Rio replied coolly.

Agatha felt tears running down her face, whether that was from the pain or heartbreak, she didn’t know.

“Goodbye, Mrs Smith,” Rio told her.

Agatha took a step forward and groaned when her leg buckled, and agonising pain spread across it. Rio was right, she couldn’t run after her like this.

“Rio, baby, don’t do this,” Agatha pleaded. “Don’t leave me.”

It reminded her of when the situation had been reversed. When she’d gotten the first round of texts, and she was trying to tell Rio that she should get a new partner. And Rio had begged her not to leave her.

Rio’s mask of detachment didn’t waver.

“Please, my love,” Agatha choked out. “Please.” Even though her body screamed at her not to, Agatha took another step closer.

Rio reached into her pocket and grabbed another knife. “Take another step and the next ones in your heart.”

“Do it,” Agatha replied without missing a beat. “It’s yours anyway.”

She saw her wife’s eyes flick upwards before something smacked her in the head.

Agatha had been knocked out cold.

Chapter 39

Chapter Notes

Rio Vidal, you've got some explaining to do girl (this is the past three days from Rio's pov)

TW: child abuse

See the end of the chapter for more notes

Rio blinked. “Where did you get these from?”

Marina smiled. “Where do you think?”

They were pictures of Nicky. There were photos of him at school, eating breakfast in his home, out at a restaurant with Wanda, in Central Park with Agatha and Rio.

“Someone is watching the boy at all hours of every day. He’s even been here.”

Rio’s head snapped up. “How?” She all but demanded.

Marina’s smile didn’t waver. “He has a friend at school, he even learnt Spanish for her when she moved here just recently. It was quite sweet actually.” Marina shrugged. “Anyway, we’re using her as well as many other people. She’s been instructed to kill him if we say so.”

Rio’s eyes widened. “You would use a little girl to kill another child?”

Marina stared at her as if it were obvious.

“Why…why would she do that?”

“We’ve told her if she doesn’t follow instructions, then we’d kill her parents back in Mexico…we haven’t told her that they’re already dead…but what does it matter.”

Rio could only blink at her. Marina was sick in the fucking head.

But was that what they were doing with Nicky? Was he already dead, and she was just saying that to get Rio to do whatever they wanted her to do…whatever that was.

“How do I know he’s not already dead?” Rio asked.

“You don’t,” Marina answered simply.

“Then why would I-”

“Would you risk it?” Marina cut her off. “You’d be killing your wife’s only child, the love of her life. She would never be able to forgive you, and you’d lose them both.” Marina pulled out her phone.

She fiddled with it momentarily before the room filled with Nicky’s cries. He was screaming and wailing at the top of his lungs. Rio winced. If her hands weren’t handcuffed, she would’ve covered her ears because she’d never heard a more horrifying sound in her life.

“Please,” Rio pleaded. “Stop it.”

Marina didn’t. She let the sound play on.

“And guess what, I can add this,” Marina continued. She tapped more buttons, and the next thing Rio knew, she heard:

“Mami! Mami, it hurts.”

That did it for Rio. Tears poured down her face as that sentence repeated.

“Mami, you can stop this! Stop it!”

“Stop it!” Rio screamed herself.

This time Marina complied. She let out a low whistle. “Technology has come a long way. You just need someone’s voice, and you can manipulate it to say anything. That’s how you get masterpieces like that!”

“What do you want?” Rio snapped.

Marina narrowed her eyes before she straightened up. “You to give us everything you know about the FBI. We want passwords, safehouse locations, agent names. All of it.”

Rio scoffed.

“You think I’m joking? You think I would joke when I just threatened to kill your son? Your wife’s son. I could have him killed like,” she snapped her fingers, “That. I’ve got moles in the FBI, so even if you’re thinking ‘Nicky will be fine, he’s probably tucked away in a safehouse somewhere,’ I have that safehouse location.”

“If you’ve got moles, why do you need me?” Rio shot back.

“Because you know far more than they’ll ever know, princess. Plus, this is way easier.”

Rio wiped at her face with her shoulder. They had her. Now she was going to be a rat betraying her country and her job because she couldn’t let anything happen to Nicky, wouldn’t. The Rio Vidal, before she joined The Smith’s Programme, would never have dreamed of doing such a thing. She would compartmentalise, detach, and let them kill an innocent boy before she betrayed her government.

But now Rio’s heart was full and beating. The art of detachment, which was once her only way of life, was a foreign language to her.

“Okay,” Rio whispered.

Marina grinned. “Atta girl. You should get some rest; you’ve got a long day of government secret sharing ahead of you tomorrow.”

Rio stared at her.

“What? I’m not a pure evil,” Marina laughed. She clapped her hands three times, and the door opened.

A man Rio had never seen before came in.

“Put her with the other one.”

The man nodded, and before Rio could think, another needle was jammed into her arm.

***

Rio woke up with a wince. Her arm was throbbing. Everything felt slow…too slow, like the world had been put in slow motion. She didn’t want to think about how many drugs were probably in her system right now.

They’d moved her once more. As Rio’s consciousness returned, she started to make out the room. It was smaller than the first one she’d been in; the walls were grey and there was a carpet. It was white and covered with various large patches of dried blood.

She was also handcuffed to a wall again.

“You scared me for a second there,” a soft voice said. “You’ve been out for a while.”

Rio forced her head to move in the direction of the voice.

“Isabella?” Rio blinked.

The other woman shot up from where she was slumped against the wall she was handcuffed to. “You know me?"

“Yes,” Rio replied.

The real Isabella Alonso, last year's Miss America beauty pageant winner. Her wife had killed the fake one when the real one had been found out to be missing a few hours before.

She was missing no more.

“What…” Rio tried because she was finding it difficult to speak. “What do they want from you?”

Isabella shrugged. “I don’t know, they don’t speak to me.”

Rio thought, even now, even covered in dried blood and dirt, that Isabella looked beautiful. She truly was Miss America.

“How…how long have you been here for?”

Isabella shrugged again. “I don’t know.”

The door rattling pulled Rio’s attention off her.

It opened to reveal a little girl with two cups of water. She walked in slowly, her head of long, thick, wavy light brown hair swaying as she walked. Her eyes were a deep blue. Rio almost sobbed. In person, she looked so much like Agatha.

“Valentina?” Rio whispered as she handed her the water.

She knew what Nicky’s friend looked like. He would show them photos of the two of them on playdates whenever he had the chance.

“It’s…it’s Noa,” she squeaked.

Nicky had been teaching her well then. She’d thought to reply in English first.

Rio nodded. “Es hermoso.” It’s beautiful.

Noa smiled. “Gracias.”

Rio noticed the huge bruise on her arm then. It seemed Noa had seen her look at it too because she hid her arm behind her back and walked over to Isabella with the other cup. Once she was done, she left the room without another word.

Rio decided then that even if she was fated to die and couldn’t escape, she would help Noa to. She didn’t know how, but she would if it were the last thing she did.

***

Rio didn’t know how many days it had been since she’d been kidnapped. She hadn’t seen the light of day since Agatha’s birthday. Her days consisted of being trapped in a room with Isabella, sat at a table writing out passwords and data, and trying to talk to Noa as much as possible whenever the little girl came in to give them food or water.

Rio would try to make her laugh or smile whenever she could because every time the girl returned, she’d have a new bruise on her arm or face. Why were they hurting her? What had she done? They weren’t even hurting Rio to her surprise.

The only person hurting Rio was herself. She’d cut her palm with the glass she’d dropped when they snuck up on her to kidnap her. She remembered that fact after they’d stopped sedating her so frequently. She would dig into the cuts to ground her, to stop her spinning out of control, and the cuts would reopen. Daniel had bandaged her hand when they noticed.

“You can’t write if you’re injured,” he’d told her.

Rio was going to kill him and every person who had laid a hand on Noa and Isabella.

She was back at her usual table, in the usual room, in the usual handcuffs as she wrote the next set of codes Marina had asked for, when she caught sentences of what appeared to be a heated conversation.

“You underestimate how much she loves her,” Daniel whispered. “The woman told us and our eyes in the FBI have reported the same thing. She’s like a madwoman. She doesn’t sleep; she doesn’t even eat. She’s just waiting until they find her, and then what? She’ll come.”

“Our eyes will throw them off the scent. They won’t find us or her before she’s dead,” Marina replied.

“We need to do something. We need her to get her to stop looking.”

Marina huffed loudly. “Think of something, then do it.” Rio heard her walking away.

She smiled because, of course, her wife was looking for her, of course she wouldn’t stop until she’d found Rio. She was also slightly annoyed at Agatha for not eating or sleeping. Rio was missing, but that didn’t mean she stopped looking after herself.

Rio didn’t know how long it had been until Daniel returned.

“It’s you’re lucky day, princess. We’re going on a field trip.”

***

The next thing Rio knew, she was in a car, blindfolded and handcuffed with two people on either side of her. It was unnecessary, she wasn’t going anywhere, the threat that they would harm Nicky in any way had stopped any thought about her trying to escape.

The car drew to a stop, and she was yanked out of the car. It felt nice to be outside again. The air was warm and fresh, and she could feel the sun on her face. She hadn’t realised how stuffy the place they were keeping her in was until she drank in the air.

She was tugged forward and made to walk for what felt like forever. When they pulled the blindfold off, Rio was in a warehouse, and the temperature had dropped significantly. They uncuffed her and instructed her to stand in a corridor made up of high wooden planks that reached the ceiling.

Daniel put two knives in her pocket. “If you use them on yourself, we’ll kill the boy,” he told her.

She wanted to ask him what they were for, but kept her mouth shut.

“Don’t look at anything but the wall in front of you until you hear that voice, or we’ll kill the boy.”

“What voice?” Rio had to ask that one.

“You’ll know it when you hear it. You’ll know exactly what to do,” he grinned, then he disappeared behind the planks of wood.

The minutes droned on, and Rio tried to think of the reason why they were making her do this when she heard it. That voice, that beautiful voice.

“Baby?”

Rio froze. No. No, it’s not you. Please don’t let it be you.

She turned slowly and lo and behold, there she was. Agatha. Rio couldn’t help but notice she looked different. Thinner, she had dark bags around her eyes and her long hair, although in a ponytail, was a mess like she hadn’t brushed it in days.

Agatha lit up when she saw Rio’s face. “You’re okay!”

But she wasn’t, far from it.

“What are you doing here?” Rio asked, she couldn’t keep the tremble out of her voice because she knew.

We need to get her to stop looking.

That was Rio’s job. That’s why she was there. To say or do something to make her wife never look her in the eyes again.

When Agatha stepped towards her, she stepped back because she couldn't do this, couldn’t hurt her wife. She’d rather die.

She’d told her wife to leave, and to no surprise to Rio, she flat out refused. Agatha picked up on the fact that something was wrong immediately, and Rio wanted nothing more than to tell her. Tell her about Nicky, about the Serpiente’s, about Isabella and Noa.

“I’ll protect you,” Agatha told her.

I know you usually can, but not from this.

She could see her wife getting angrier the more she refused to go with her.

“I’m not leaving you. Not unless someone killed me, and even in death, I wouldn’t. I’d haunt you in my ghost form,” Agatha quipped.

Even at her lowest, her wife would still find ways to tease and make jokes. Rio wanted nothing more than to smile and laugh, but the situation was too dire, too awful to even consider it.

Rio couldn’t do this. She couldn’t stand there and listen to her wife ask her to leave with her and not be able to comply, not be able to do exactly as she said, because Rio always did. Like she said, Agatha could ask her to rip out her own kidney, and she’d do it without a second thought.

So, refusing her? It was Rio’s idea of hell. Consequences be damned Rio was done with this.

“If you won’t leave, then I will.”

She turned to do just that and felt Agatha’s hand on her arm. She could’ve cried, to feel her wife’s touch again after however long without it, felt like Rio’s body was alive again. That she’d been dead and now she was being brought back to the living. But Agatha couldn’t touch her otherwise, Rio would do something silly like try to leave with her.

The only thing Rio could think of to get her to stop was to pretend to harm her. She didn’t want to, she really didn’t, but she brought her fist up and swung.

Just as Rio knew she would, Agatha blocked it with ease. The look on her wife’s face, however, the horror and betrayal would be etched into Rio’s mind forever.

Agatha kept questioning her, kept touching her, and Rio really did have to hit her to get her to let go.

“I’m leaving,” Rio told her after the last time Agatha grabbed her wrist.

She turned to leave once more, and this time, when Agatha spun her around, she kissed her. She fucking kissed her, and all Rio wanted to do was sink into it. Agatha’s lips were so soft, so warm, so perfect in every way imaginable. Rio didn’t know if she’d ever get the opportunity to kiss her wife again.

This was a gift, a gift she couldn’t keep.

She pushed Agatha away before she got lost in it, before she did something stupid. She could feel the tears collecting in her eyes.

“Don’t do that,” Rio got out.

“Why not?” And then Agatha was stepping closer, and Rio couldn’t bring herself to step back again. She wanted her wife to touch her, to kiss her. She never wanted to be apart from her, not now, not ever.

“Why not, sweetheart?” Agatha asked softly.

Rio was a goner. Her wife stepped into her orbit and wrapped her arms around her. What was the point, right? Of fighting her, of trying to get her to leave. Because Agatha wouldn’t, and neither would Rio.

She would never leave her; she promised her that.

“You’re never going to let me go, are you?” Rio spoke into the silence moments later, tears slipping down her face.

The reply came quickly. “Never.” She felt her wife run her fingers through her hair. “Whatever is going on with you, you’re going to tell me, and we’re going to deal with it together. Like always.”

The realisation hit Rio like a ton of bricks because there was a point. Nicky. His life, that’s what was going on with her, that’s why she couldn’t go with Agatha. Rio had forgotten in the haze of it all, seeing Agatha again, touching her, kissing her.

We need to get her to stop looking.

That was Rio’s job. To do something so hurtful that her wife would never look for again. So that Nicky could be safe.

She remembered the knives in her pockets and knew exactly why she’d been given them. The answer was clear as day now.

Rio let out a sob as she discreetly reached into her pocket as her wife’s grip around her tightened. If Rio was going to do this, she needed to detach or at least appear detached. She could do that; she had to do that.

It was the only way.

The knife was in her hand now, just before Agatha’s thigh.

I’m sorry, I’m sorry, I love you, I’m sorry.

Rio plunged the knife in.

The look on Agatha’s face when she realised what she had done would haunt Rio until the end of time.

“I don’t…I don’t understand,” Agatha got out.

“You can’t chase me down if you can’t run,” Rio replied in what she hoped was an even tone.

Rio thought she might throw up. To look at Agatha with blood pouring down her leg, knowing she was the one who had done that, threatened to kill her. She wanted to run towards her, call her an ambulance, apologise until she couldn’t breathe.

She couldn’t.

She had to stand there and pretend that none of this was bothering her when that couldn’t be further from the truth.

Tears started running down Agatha’s face, and Rio needed this to be over.

“Goodbye, Mrs Smith.” She couldn’t say her name; Rio didn’t deserve to say it again after what she’d just done.

When Agatha took a step and groaned, Rio had to force herself not to wince at the devastating sound. Her body twitched to surge forward and help her, but Rio forced herself to stay put.

“Rio, baby, don’t do this.”

Baby. Don’t call me that, please don’t. I no longer deserve it. Hate me. Please hate me. Stop fighting for me.

“Don’t leave me.”

I don’t want to! Rio wanted to say, wanted to scream at the top of her lungs.

“Please, my love,” Agatha cried. “Please.”

Her wife took another step, and Rio reached for the second knife. Her hand was trembling, but she tightened her grip around the knife to stop it.

“Take another step and the next ones in your heart,” Rio forced out because that had to work, right? That would hurt so much that Agatha would be so disgusted she’d be done with her for good.

But it didn’t.

“Do it,” Agatha replied without missing a beat. “It’s yours anyway.”

Rio could cry, would cry if she were allowed to, because her heart belonged to Agatha as well. Rio figured it what stop beating after this. It would fossilise, and she would live out the rest of her days without it until her death sentence came.

Because after today, Rio might as well be dead.

Daniel came out of seemingly nowhere, a wooden plank raised above his head, before he smacked Agatha over the head with it.

Her wife crashed to the ground with a thud.

“No!” Rio screamed, surging forward.

She could harm her wife (and only to protect her); nobody else on planet earth could.

She rushed over to Agatha and fell to the floor, putting Agatha’s head on her lap as she brushed through her dark waves. Tears slipped down her face and onto her wife’s cheeks, she hastily wiped them away.

“Up,” Daniel demanded. “You did well, we’re done here.”

Rio ignored him and fished around in her wife’s back pocket for a phone. She found it, clicked it on and sent a message to Jen and Alice telling them to track Agatha’s phone and call an ambulance.

“What are you doing?” Daniel yelled. He reached for her, and Rio held out the knife she didn’t use to get him to back off.

“I’m coming with you, okay! But I’m not leaving until I know someone’s coming to get her.”

Daniel scoffed. “You don’t have a choice. Get up before I hurt you.”

“Fucking kill me then because I’m not leaving her like this!” Rio shot back.

Daniel said nothing.

When it was confirmed that help was on the way, Rio slid Agatha’s phone back into her pocket and kissed her twice. Once for her, once for Nicky, before she rested her head down gently on the ground.

I love you, I love you, I’m sorry, I love you.

She got up and handed the knife back to Daniel, who yanked her by the arm and dragged her away from her unconscious wife.

Chapter End Notes
