Chapter 40

Chapter Notes

y'all have some faith in me, the angst with a happy ending tag isn't going anywhere

TW: mentions of child trafficking, sex trafficking, and SA (no SA happens)

See the end of the chapter for more notes

She was in a hospital. Agatha fucking hated hospitals.

It was the smell more than anything. It was unsettling, like it was trying to be clean, but instead the smell of antiseptic was just a big cloud of fog trying to conceal all of the diseases and sicknesses that filled every corridor, every room, every corner.

She was attached to a drip; whatever painkiller they were giving her filling her bloodstream. There was a huge lump on her head that was concealed behind a bandage, and her thigh had been stitched up.

Agatha hadn’t felt so trapped in days, and that was saying something. Between MO and the safehouse, the hospital was by far the worst enclosure she had found herself in.

“Agatha?”

Her eyes snapped to green.

And to make things fucking worse Wanda was there.

Jen and Alice had taken Nicky to the vending machine to buy him some snacks.

“Have you been listening to me?”

“No.”

Wanda sighed. “I said they should be letting you out soon.”

Good. Because then she could finally return to trying to find Rio. She’d been in the hospital for far too long now, not being able to do a thing. She’d tried to escape on multiple occasions, but there were FBI agents crawling about the place, making sure she stayed put.

It had happened more times than she’d like to admit, her trying to escape and agents dragging her back to her room, kicking and screaming. She’d started losing track of time, the pain in her leg, plus her concussion, plus the painkillers kept knocking her out. She wanted them to lay off the painkillers because of it, but the doctors told her it would make her feel better.

That was fucking bullshit because no matter what drug they gave her Agatha wouldn’t be fine until she found Rio again.

“Where do you want to go after this? We can’t stay in New York, it’s not safe.”

We as if they were in this together, as if they were a team. The only team Agatha belonged to included her wife, her two best friends, and her son. Wanda’s were not included.

“I’m going to find Rio.”

Wanda’s jaw dropped. “You…you still want to find her?”

If Agatha was the one who had been concussed, why was her ex acting so slow?

“I just said that, didn’t I?” Agatha snapped.

“But…but she,” Wanda spluttered. “She fucking stabbed you!”

“So?”

Wanda gaped at her. “So…so why would you want anything to do with her?”

“Oh…I don’t know because she’s my fucking wife,” Agatha replied sarcastically.

“Who stabbed you!” Wanda shot back.

Agatha rolled her eyes.

“Do you understand how fucking insane that is? The woman who supposedly loves you fucking stabbed you!”

“And she also told Alice and Jen to come get me and call me an ambulance. So, what does that tell you? That she didn’t fucking want to. Jesus, Wanda, use your brain.”

“I…” Wanda started, then stopped. “You love her too much. It’ll kill you.”

“Let it,” Agatha replied without missing a beat.

Wanda scoffed. “What about Nicky? Your son. You’d let yourself get killed for her? You’d leave him without his mother, for her?”

Now that stopped Agatha dead in her tracks. Nicky. No, she wouldn’t leave him. That boy was everything to her, everything to each of his mothers. Wanda, her, Rio…

Rio.

Agatha shot up.

That was it. That was what they had on her, her son. Rio would rather die than let anything happen to him, just as Agatha would.

“Wanda,” Agatha said without looking at her. “You’re a fucking genius.”

“I…what?” The redhead stuttered.

***

Rio had her eyes closed, her head against the wall as tears slipped down her face. She’d just woken up from her fifth round of sedatives. They’d told her she was being hysterical and needed a time out…multiple.

After she’d stabbed Agatha and Daniel had handcuffed her and yanked her towards the car, she couldn’t stop crying. How had she done that? She’d left Agatha by herself in the middle of fucking nowhere bleeding out and unconscious.

She would’ve been fine with just the stabbing, Rio made sure she hadn’t punctured any fatal areas, all she would need was some stitches. But then Daniel had knocked her out. What for? He didn’t need to do that.

Had Rio killed her? Had Rio killed her own wife?

She would never know because she would never see Agatha again.

She did try after a while to run back to the warehouse to make sure Agatha was okay, but Daniel grabbed her, picked her up and dragged her towards the car, kicking and screaming.

How could I do that? Rio asked herself often.

To protect her.

But did I?

Rio didn’t think so.

“Are you okay?” Isabella asked from the other side of the room.

“No,” Rio replied flatly. The drugs made her mouth move faster than her brain had the chance to process, so she couldn’t lie if she tried.

“Want to talk about it?”

Rio shook her head. She couldn’t talk about it. Her thoughts were vile enough, she didn’t need to hear what an awful person she was from another person’s mouth.

“Okay,” Isabella replied. “But if it’s about your wife, don’t beat yourself up about it,” she shrugged. “You did what you had to do.”

Rio opened her eyes at that. “You know?”

Isabella nodded. “Nobody keeps their mouth shut in this place. Everyone talks about ‘The Princess and her mad wife.’”

Rio laughed at that, wiping at the tears on her face.

She sniffled. “I had to hurt her.”

Isabella nodded slowly. “But you didn’t want,” she replied as if it were the truth, which it was.

“No. I’d rather hurt myself than hurt her.”

“And you’re scared she won’t forgive you, and that’s why you’re upset?” Isabella asked.

Rio let out a wet laugh, shaking her head. “That’s the worst part. I did it, and she still wanted me. So, it’s like, what did I do it for?”

“A reason that made sense at the time. A reason that has probably saved her from why they needed you to do it in the first place.”

Rio pressed her lips into a thin line as she took in Isabella’s words.

“She must love you an awful lot. You’re lucky to be loved like that,” Isabella told her.

Rio pressed the heels of her hands into her eyes. “But that’s the problem. I stabbed her. I broke skin and drew blood. You’re not supposed to…you’re not supposed to still love someone after that.”

“But that’s the thing about love,” Isabella replied. “One choice doesn’t stop it. It continues to flow at full force even when you feel it shouldn’t. It doesn’t just turn off.”

“But shouldn’t it?”

Rio couldn’t help but feel like Wanda. The ginger bitch had gotten away with so much and yet Agatha still loved her. She didn’t want her wife to forgive her for this. Rio hoped that once she was dead, all Agatha would feel was resentment. That she would remember the pain and the stitches and the hospital (her wife hated hospitals) and feel all of that instead of her love for Rio.

Because Rio no longer deserved it.

***

Everyone had returned to the safehouse, leaving Agatha alone in the hospital. She begged them to take her with them, but her doctor refused, telling her she still needed at least one more night there.

The shadows from the trees outside her window kept moving, crawling about her room as if they were evil spirits ready to snatch her soul. As much as Rio liked to disagree, Agatha didn’t scare easy. It was just the fact that she was in a hospital at night alone.

Now, the sudden blare of car horns that she’d been accustomed to after a life living in the city made her jump. Agatha hated this, she wanted to go home, she wanted to be with Nicky, she wanted…

She wanted Rio.

Her eyes snapped to her open hospital room when a shadow flashed across the threshold. She reached under the covers for her gun. She was supposed to be protected by the agents outside, but after everything that had happened, Agatha had a theory…no, she was certain…

There were moles in the FBI.

She wasn’t sure if they would be after her; it was clear Rio’s kidnappers weren’t. At the warehouse, they had every opportunity to kill her, and they hadn’t.

Agatha curled her finger around the trigger, ready for if she needed it, when the light in her doorway fluctuated again.

She snapped her gun up when a man appeared in the threshold. He stared at her, his hands up in surrender. In the dim light, it was hard to make out the man’s face. He had a mix of dark brown and grey hair and what looked like a goatee.

“I’m not here to hurt you,” the man told her.

Agatha scoffed. “Like I’m supposed to believe that.”

“I swear it, Agatha.”

How did he know her name?

He stepped further into the room, even though she still had her gun pointed at him.

She caught the glint of deep brown in his eyes as they reflected the light off the lamp posts outside. They weren’t the brown eyes she’d fallen in love with, but they were…similar.

Agatha squeezed the trigger slightly. “What do you want?” She snapped.

“The same thing you do,” Rio’s father replied simply.

She knew it was him; Vidal eyes were so distinguishable. Agatha thought of Rio and the pictures she’d shown her of her Abuela, and the similarities were so clear it was almost frightening.

“To save my daughter, both of them.”

Agatha furrowed her eyebrows. Both of them? Rio had never mentioned having a sister.

“I tried to warn you,” he continued. “I thought that text would’ve scared you.”

Agatha’s hand clenched around her gun and she damn well near pulled it. “You were the one texting me?”

“I texted you once three months ago. I never texted you again. I thought you would care more about my daughter’s safety than whatever relationship you had built with her.”

“I…” Agatha started, then stopped.

This was her fucking fault. If she hadn’t been selfish, if she hadn’t been weak and not crumbled the second Rio begged her not to leave her then none of this would’ve fucking happened.

Fucking stupid.

Rio’s father stepped closer regardless of the gun trained on him. “It doesn’t matter now, we need to get her back, both of them. The Serpientes, they are terrible people. Every inhumane thing you can think of they have a hand in it. Child trafficking, sex slaves, you name it, and they’ve done it.”

Agatha swallowed. To think of Rio being stripped of her identity and sold to the highest bidder made bile climb up her throat.

“I know that’s what they plan to do with Isabella, make her a sex worker. I am still unsure what they want with Rio.”

“Isabella?” Agatha questioned. Like…Isabella, last year's Mrs America’s winner? She was Rio’s sister?

Rio’s father nodded. “I know where the Serpiente’s headquarters are. You must go there and get them.”

Agatha lowered her gun slightly. “How?”

Rio’s father sighed. “I used to be their leader.”

Agatha snapped her gun back up. Rio’s father had just told her the Serpientes were terrible people, and yet he had been their leader? What. The. Fuck.

“I know what you’re thinking, but it was not that way when I was in control. When it started to go south, I left. For my wife, for Rio. They would expect her to be something I never wanted her to grow up to be. So, I hid her, and they killed my wife.”

Agatha stared at him. She didn’t trust him, not even a little bit. But if he knew where Rio was, she wouldn’t do anything to him…yet.

“Why do you want to protect her now? You’re thirty three years fucking late don’t you think?” Agatha stated.

“I’ve been watching her all those years, looking out for her in ways she’ll never know. You have to stay away from the people you love in order to protect them. You do that…with Nicholas.”

Agatha jerked her head back at the mention of her son. “How do you-?”

“Like I said, I’ve been looking out for her,” Rio’s father cut her off. “And recently that has also meant watching you.”

“If you’ve been watching us, then why didn’t you see this coming?” Agatha snapped.

“I did. I warned you,” he replied.

And now Agatha was pissed. “Then why the fuck did you let it happen? Why did you let them fucking take her?!”

Rio’s father simply stared at her before he continued. “You can’t trust anyone at the FBI apart from your two friends and Agent Calderu. Have them look after Nicholas while you get Rio and Isabella.”

Agatha glared at him. She was aware he’d completely dodged her question, but getting Rio was far more important. “You want me to infiltrate the Serpiente headquarters…alone?”

He nodded. “I trust you won’t need backup. You are a good agent…one of the best, and you have enough rage in you, for what they did to Rio, to the both of you to get the job done.” He smiled for he first time since he stepped foot in the room. “Plus, you’ll have some extra help should you need it.”

“How do you know any of this? How are you even in here?” Agatha blurted out.

“I have help,” Rio’s father replied with no further context. “Now, you know what to do, Agatha. Protect your son, get my daughters.” He turned to leave.

“Why can’t you do it?” She had to ask, she would never let anyone else rescue Rio, but she wanted to know why her father had no intention of doing so.

He stopped in his tracks. “You love her?” He asked instead of answering.

“More than you ever will,” Agatha replied without missing a beat.

“Then it’s best you do it,” Rio’s father replied. “You’ll have her location when you wake up tomorrow. Get some sleep, Agatha. You’ll need it.”

“But why do they want her now?” Agatha blurted out again because she still had more questions.

“Sleep, Agatha.”

Rio’s father disappeared through the threshold.

***

“Isa…” Rio started.

What she assumed to have been yesterday, after Noa had come in, fed her (physically because Rio’s arm’s were dead to the word. She noticed them beginning to stop working after she’d had that conversation with Isabella, like they were trying to paralyse her), and given her water, they knocked her out again.

She’d woken up to the sound of Isabella crying.

“Isabella, what’s wrong?” Rio asked, shuffling as close to her as her bounds would allow her. The distance of the room still separated them a great deal.

Isabella hadn’t cried once since she’d been here.

Glassy, dark brown eyes looked up, tears streaming down her face. “I finally know what they want with me.”

Panic exploded in Rio’s chest. She said nothing, allowing Isabella to continue if she wanted to.

“Sex work,” Isabella said bitterly.

Rio’s body went stiff. Not on her fucking watch.

“Have they…” Rio trailed off. She needed to word this right. “Did they touch you?” Rio asked softly.

Isabella shook her head. “Not yet. But they will.”

“I won’t let it,” Rio replied firmly. “They won’t lay a finger on you, I swear it.”

Isabella offered her a small smile. “I appreciate it, Rio, really. But there is no hope for me. You’ll be dead soon.”

And she hadn’t sugar-coated it because they both knew.

But Rio meant what she said. She shuffled closer until her chains were physically yanking her back. “Listen to me, I-”

She cut herself off when a commotion started up outside. Heated conversations in Spanish were muffled behind the closed door until said door opened.

“Get her and let’s go,” Marina said as Daniel stormed into the room towards Rio. “She’s here.”

Chapter End Notes

Chapter 41

Chapter Notes

as requested, many bodies shall be hitting floors.

(this chapter is slightly more gruesome than any other mission so bare that in mind if you don't like blood)

See the end of the chapter for more notes

The Serpiente’s headquarters were a huge mansion in upstate New York. It was in a lovely little neighbourhood, with lovely little neighbours who would never suspect they were living next to notorious criminals.

Rio’s father told Agatha that they were keeping Rio in the basement and the best way for her to enter the house would be right through the front door…as a prostitute. He’d told her that the members not in the basement would be low-level and less likely to recognise her; they’d probably only know her name. Plus, it was common to have men and women in and out purely for sex.

Once Agatha had relayed the plan to Jen, Alice and Lilia, she had a very heartfelt goodbye with Nicky, telling him she had a mission she needed to take care of and to be good for his Aunts. Agatha left for the location, Lilia on her tail.

Agatha pulled to a stop a few houses down from the Serpiente’s mansion. It was a white building with a green roof that reminded her of rusted iron; it had pointed turrets on either side of the wide house, and there were many, many windows. The house was four levels (not including the basement).

“Fuck me,” Agatha muttered.

Now she wasn’t nervous, but that was a big house and there was only one of her…well, one of her until she found Rio. She was certain a highly skilled agent against amateurs would be fine, but like she said…

“Jesus Christ, that’s a big house.”

She checked her appearance one last time in her car mirror. Agatha was wearing light-washed jeans, a V-neck tight-fitted long-sleeved button-up white blouse that revealed her black lace bra and black leather boots. She was also wearing a decent amount of makeup and her signature deep red lipstick because she had to look the part.

Her hair was down and wavy, but she had a hair band on her wrist for when things would get…messy later. She’d also painted her nails a deep red to match her lipstick, but that was more from being bored out of her mind sitting at the hospital, ready to be released than anything else.

When Agatha was happy she had her gun, three knives, and com, she hopped out of the car and made her way to the house, nodding at Lilia when she passed.

“Shout if you need backup,” Lilia told her in her ear.

“Will do,” Agatha replied as she walked up the steps to the house.

She knocked three times then waited.

Moments later, a man appeared at the door. Agatha smiled that smile of hers, she used on Rio whenever she wanted her on her knees. The man’s throat bobbled.

“Hi,” Agatha said, her voice dripping with seduction. “I heard my services were needed.”

The man with light brown hair and a snake tattoo snaking up his neck dropped his gaze to her cleavage. If she were allowed, she’d kill him right here and now. Instead, she continued to smile.

“Are you gonna let a girl in? It’s cold out here.” (It wasn’t).

The man nodded his head frantically and stepped aside.

Well, that was easy.

He walked her into the house and past the kitchen, where four men sat around a table. They continued down the corridor until they reached the stairs, where she saw a shut door that definitely led to the basement.

Bingo.

She took a step towards it when a group of men and women burst through the door. In the chaos, the man who had let her in tugged her up the stairs. Of course, she could’ve freed herself if she wanted to, but that wouldn’t be smart. She’d have to take on that cluster of people all at once, and what if one escaped, ran downstairs and told them she was here? Then they’d try to move Rio before she got to her.

Agatha, for now, had to be smart.

The man tugged her up more flights of stairs; many of the rooms she passed were shut or only had one person in them. More than once, if the person in the room saw them, they’d say something like, ‘Pedro, give her to me when you’re done,’ and Pedro would laugh, and Agatha would make a mental note to return to those rooms and kill them.

When they hit the fourth floor, Pedro, finally, pushed a door open and let her into a room she guessed was his. Agatha looked about his room briefly until her eyes landed on him again. Pedro had stripped off his black t-shirt, and she had to suppress the urge to grimace at the half-naked man in front of her.

“What’s your name, baby girl?” Pedro asked as he began unbuckling his belt. “I want to know whose name I’ll be moaning.”

Agatha was going to throw up.

“Agatha Harkness,” she replied.

Pedro nodded absentmindedly, too busy taking off his trousers for the information to register. He stalked over to her in his monkey underwear, reached his hand up to touch her face until the hand stilled.

“Agatha…Harkness…?”

Agatha grinned like a shark.

Pedro opened his mouth as if to shout when Agatha jammed one of her knives into his throat. His blood began to trickle down her white shirt sleeve, and she groaned.

“Pedro, I liked this shirt! You’ve ruined it now, it was very expensive,” Agatha whined.

Pedro started to choke and gargle. “Puta.” Bitch. He got out before he spat blood at her. She felt the hot liquid on her face and exposed chest.

Agatha narrowed her eyes before shoving the knife in further until the light in Pedro’s eyes went out. She wrenched her knife free and shoved his body to the ground.

She grimaced as she wiped the blood mixed with spit off her face. Agatha didn’t mind blood, but not when it was spat at her by a man.

She kicked him once before exiting the room.

Agatha went back down the stairs to a room on the third floor of a man who had asked Pedro for her once he was done. She knocked, hiding her bloody hands behind her back.

He looked up at her in surprise. “That was quick.”

“Pedro doesn’t last long,” Agatha told him with a smile.

The man scoffed. “I told him he needed to work on that.”

“Can I come in?”

The man nodded. “Hey, what’s on your face?”

Agatha blinked at him innocently. “My face? Oh! Kool-Aid.”

The man, so horny and desperate didn’t question her again. He yanked her by the waist, pulling her towards him, seemingly to kiss her, but he paused.

“That…that doesn’t look like Kool-Aid?”

“No?” Agatha furrowed her eyebrows.

He paused, staring at her for a long moment until it appeared he had connected some dots. Again, he went to shout when Agatha jammed the same knife into this man’s throat.

“Ah, ah,” she tutted. “Can’t have people knowing I’m here yet.”

More hot blood from this man trailed down her arms, and she seriously had to ask herself what possessed her to wear white.

She removed her knife and let the man drop to the floor. She inspected her bloody hands and noticed that her nail varnish was chipped.

“Are you fucking serious? I just painted these.”

Agatha slipped out of the room and down the landing.

Adrenaline was coursing through her veins after her first two kills. It wasn’t the same type of ecstasy she felt when she could shoot at her enemy, each bullet landing exactly where she’d want them to, time and time again, but it was close enough. It felt good to use her hands to get the job done, to get all these people back who had a hand in Rio’s captivity.

As much as she wanted to go into every room and slaughter every person who had made a vulgar comment about her, she realised she couldn’t. It took too much time, and she needed to find Rio. That didn’t mean she stopped killing, though. Now covered in blood, her presence went a little less unnoticed.

She still snuck past doors. Sometimes she was successful, others a man or woman would start screaming and she’d have to knock them, slit their throat, or stab them.

Fuck me this house is big. Agatha thought when she made it to the second floor.

Now, her white shirt sleeves were mostly red, there were splatters of blood on her jeans, boots, face, exposed chest and lace bra. She looked straight out of a horror film. Agatha blew her long hair out of her face as she wiped her forehead with the back of her bloody hand.

Jesus, why is killing people so exhausting? Agatha was sweating so much she could fill a bathtub.

She scraped her hair into a high ponytail.

As soon as she was finished, she heard the creaking of floorboards and then a fist was flying towards her face. She dodged it, ducking underneath before bringing her knee up to knee the woman in the stomach. She folded over, and Agatha hit her in the back of the head with her elbow.

She contemplated leaving her there, but realised it wouldn’t be smart to have her out in the open. All the other bodies had been concealed behind closed doors. Agatha groaned before looping her arms underneath the limp body and shuffling towards the shut door to her left.

She used her elbow to push down on the door handle and dragged the unconscious woman through the threshold. She dropped her body down with a huff.

“Mierda.” Shit.

Agatha spun around to see a man reaching into his back pocket for what she assumed to be a gun. Now, that wouldn’t do. She spotted a baseball bat by the unconscious woman’s feet and grinned.

She picked it up without hesitation and swung it down on the man’s hand as he lifted his gun. It dropped to the ground, and Agatha watched as the man’s eyes widened before she sent him to a blissful sleep with one swing of the baseball bat.

She was splattered with more blood as it appeared she’d smashed the man’s skull in. She inspected the pale wood with its new red detailing.

“Huh.”

Why hadn’t someone had a baseball bat sooner? It would’ve made her life a whole lot easier.

With her new baseball bat, she exited the room, the bat swinging in her hand as she skipped down the landing.

Oh, this was fun.

She was mildly aware that her thigh was starting to hurt. Agatha figured she’d probably ripped open the stitching.

Oh well.

She was too high on adrenaline to give a fuck.

“Everything okay in there?” Lilia asked in her ear.

“Yup,” Agatha replied when she hit the first floor.

“What’s-”

“Wait, hold on,” Agatha cut her off when two women came at her.

She went to hit them with her baseball bat when one of the women kicked it out of her hand.

Oh, for fucksake.

Agatha kicked out with her right foot, connecting with one woman’s stomach whilst she shot out her fist at the other woman, punching her in the nose. Her head snapped back, and she didn’t get to see how much damage she caused because the other woman grabbed her foot.

She turned back around and used the advantage of her foot being held to push off the ground. The woman let go of her leg in surprise, and Agatha flipped midair, sticking the landing as if she were an Olympic gymnast.

The two women gaped at her.

“What?” Agatha panted. “You've never seen an FBI agent before?”

They continued to gape until she used the back of her hands to knock them out at the same time. Once they were out cold, Agatha started fanning underneath her arms. It had been a very long time since she’d done so much physical fighting all at once. She missed using her gun, stupid having to be covert so as not to alert people of her presence.

She picked up her bat again. “Go on, Lilia,” Agatha told the older woman as she made her way down the steps and (finally) onto the ground floor.

She yanked the door of the basement open, pleased when it gave way and hadn’t been locked.

“What’s the situation looking like?” Lilia asked as Agatha ran down the stairs to the door at the end.

“I just got to the basement.”

“Only?” Lilia asked in alarm.

“Yes, Lilia. I had to deal with some shit,” Agatha replied as she opened the next door.

She’d entered a long corridor with grey walls and pipes running down their lengths. It was dimly lit and empty…too empty. There wasn’t a soul in sight. Had she blown her cover? Agatha swore she was being careful…but then she’d killed or knocked out next to twenty-five people by now. Can you really be covert about that?

She shrugged and started down the corridor, baseball bat still firmly clutched in bloody fingers. Once at the end, she came up to another corridor. She stuck her head out to check if it was safe and…

BANG!

A bullet almost blew her head off. Guess her presence was known after all. She pulled her head back, yanked her gun out of it’s holster and turned it down the corridor without poking her head out again, she didn’t need to, she’d seen the man’s location now.

She pulled the trigger, heard the groan of the man when the bullet hit, and the thud of his body as it crashed to the ground.

Agatha wasn’t happy about that. She’d much rather they didn’t know where she was exactly; that gunshot just told everyone.

She ran down the next corridor.

“Everything okay? I heard a gun.” Lilia asked.

“Fine,” Agatha replied as she shoved the door she’d approached open.

Two sets of eyes locked onto her from where they’d been standing behind it. They grinned as if they’d been expecting her.

“Hi, boys,” Agatha smiled. “Are you here for me?”

“La esposa loca de la princesa esta buena.” The princess’s crazy wife is hot. One of the men told his friend.

Is that what they were calling her now? Kind of had a ring to it.

Thank god for being an attractive woman, because when the men just stared at her, they had no chance when Agatha swung the baseball bat above her head and swung. She stepped over the now unconscious bodies and further into the surprisingly empty room until she got to the door, opened it:

“Oh, what the fuck?!” Agatha grumbled when she hit yet another long corridor.

This place was a maze, and she’d seen no sign of Rio. The next person Agatha came across, she was going to make sure to question them instead of immediately knocking them out or killing them. She rolled her eyes before moving along the next corridor.

She pressed her body up against the wall when she heard footsteps shuffling down the corridor over. Agatha waited for the footsteps to draw closer before she shot out, snatched the woman by her shirt and forced her against the wall. She got out her knife and pressed it against her throat.

“Do you know who I am?” Agatha asked in a low voice.

The woman nodded frantically.

“Good. Then you know what I want, where is she?”

The woman’s petrified expression seemed to vanish at that. Agatha narrowed her eyes before the woman launched a ball of spit at her face.

Why the fuck was everyone spitting at her?!

She took great pleasure in backhanding the woman, her face snapping to the side from where she’d hit her.

She wiped at her cheek with the hand holding her bat before she snarled, “Wanna try that again?”

“I’m not telling you shit!” The woman spat. “We own the princess now; you can’t have her, she’s ours!”

Now that just wouldn’t do.

Agatha pressed the blade into the woman’s neck until beads of blood started to appear. “No. Rio is not yours, she’s mine,” Agatha nodded. “And you’ve had her for far too long now, and I don’t like sharing.”

The woman started choking and gasping for air.

“I’ve been referred to as her mad wife around here. Is that true?”

The woman, now desperate to cling on to her life, started nodding frantically again.

Agatha grinned, the woman’s blood slipping down her wrist to join the blood of her dead companions.

“Would you like to find out why?”

The woman shook her head as best she could.

“Perfect!” Agatha said, her grin never wavering. She pulled her knife away, pocketing it before she dragged the woman off the wall by her hair down the new corridor. “You’re going to take me to my wife then.”

***

About five corridors later, the woman told her to stop outside a door. Agatha glanced at her.

“Well, go on then. Open it.”

The woman went to do so before Agatha yanked her by the hair.

“And if you’ve trapped me, I’ll break your spine before they get the chance to do anything to me…understood?”

The other woman nodded.

“Fantastic! Go on then.”

The woman pulled the door open, and Agatha laid eyes on what seemed like an aeroplane bunker…minus the planes. It was just a large open space with a few cars dotted around here and there.

Huh?

How fucking big was the place? All of this was just lying around under the entirety of upstate New York? It was like they’d entered another dimension.

She pushed the woman further into the massive space.

“Where is she?” Agatha snapped when she’d scanned the space and observed that nobody was there.

The woman kept her mouth shut until:

BANG!

Agatha ducked, her hands instinctively going to cover her head, releasing the grasp on the woman. The woman didn’t hesitate to run away from her. More gunshots sounded, and as Agatha ran for cover behind a car, dropped the bat, freed one of her knives and threw it at the woman. It hit her in the back of the leg, and she tumbled to the ground.

She retrieved her gun from her holster and started firing back at her enemies, who had also hidden behind the cars littered about the place. Agatha panted against the car, gun up and ready as she waited for the next round of fire.

When it came moments later, she peeked her head up from the hood of the car, aimed her gun and:

BANG!

Bullet in the head. Dead.

“You fucking idiots!” Agatha heard a voice say. “You’re not supposed to shoot her; I need her alive!”

She furrowed her eyebrows…why the-

Her thoughts got cut off when she felt hands on her; they yanked her up by the collar of her ruined white shirt. Her feet dangled in the air as she looked down at the beefy man holding her up. She went to pull on her gun when the man shook her so violently that the gun was wrenched from her hand, sliding across the not-so-aeroplane bunker.

Oh, for fucksake.

“So, what now?” Agatha hummed. “You’re orders say you can’t kill me.”

The sound of bodies dropping a bit away caught the man’s attention, and Agatha didn’t hesitate to kick him in the balls. The man shrieked and Agatha cackled as he doubled over, putting her down, although he didn’t let go. She shoved at him as hard as she could, and the man staggered back, releasing her completely.

She slid across the floor towards her bat, considering it was closer than her gun, retrieved it, spun around with it raised to hit the man that was most likely coming back for round two, when her bat met resistance.

Her eyes snapped up to find an axe warding off the blow to the person's head.

Agatha looked down and was met with deep brown.

Hers.

Agatha took her in. She, too, was covered in a healthy amount of blood. It was splattered all over her face and on a lot more of her arms, considering her wife had on a short sleeve. She looked exhausted but buzzing with adrenaline just as Agatha was.

A slow smile spread across Rio’s lips as Agatha finally released the pressure she’d been pushing down on her wife with her bat. Rio lowered her axe, and Agatha felt her own grin sliding across her lips.

Watch out world…Agatha Harkness has her wife back.

Chapter 42

Chapter Notes

what'd that axe do???

again, this chapter is slightly more gruesome than other mission.

TW: child abuse

See the end of the chapter for more notes

She’s here.

Daniel yanked Rio’s arms up and started unlocking her cuffs. Now this was an opportunity to escape, not escape, escape, but help Isabella and Noa. If she was who Rio thought she was, the Serpentines were going to be occupied for a while.

Rio could help Isabella and Noa and potentially catch a glimpse of her wife before they carted her off or killed her.

Rio would be content if the last thing she ever saw in this life was Agatha.

Daniel had the next set of cuffs ready to place on her wrists as he uncuffed her from the ones on the wall. This was the first time he’d ever done this whilst Rio had been conscious. And although she was still drowsy from the sedatives, she was still a highly trained FBI agent. So, naturally…

Once both her hands were free, she grabbed at Daniel’s neck and head butted him in the head with every muscle in her body. His head snapped back, and he crashed to the ground. Daniel was out cold. If Rio had the time, she would’ve killed him then and there.

She fished around in his pockets for the keys for Isabella’s cuffs, there she also found a pocket knife. She scurried over to her and unlocked them.

“Rio?” Isabella asked when she was free. “Do you know what you’re doing?”

“Nope,” Rio replied before she pulled Isabella to her feet. “Just stay with me, okay?”

Isabella nodded.

“What is taking-” Marina cut herself off when she opened the door to see Rio and Isabella standing on their feet, staring at her. “Mierda.” Shit.

Marina reached into her back pocket, and before she had the chance to pull whatever she had out, Rio went for her. She knocked her off her feet, tackling her to the ground. As Marina kicked out and scratched, Rio continued to straddle her as she searched for the weapon Marina had intended to use on her.

When she freed it, it revealed itself to be a taser. Why the fuck couldn’t she have a gun? Whatever. Rio pulled out her pocket knife ready to slit Marina’s throat when a piercing scream cut through Marina’s struggles.

Rio snapped her head up to see Noa, her arm dripping with blood. She was crying as a man was carrying her down the hallway. She locked eyes with Rio and:

“Rio! Please!”

She sounded like Nicky on that voice manipulation record Marina has shown her. Rio’s heart shattered.

She didn’t think before she jammed the knife in Marina’s neck before springing up and shooting down the corridor towards Noa.

“Isabella! Come on!” Rio urged.

The previous Miss America fell in line behind her as they sprinted towards Noa. She and the man carrying her disappeared behind the door at the end of the hallway. Rio ripped it open to see Noa and the man crossing through an empty room covered in patches of dried blood before slipping behind another door.

Rio had never seen the place where she’d been held captive, only her cell and the room where she would share government secrets. Rio was starting to believe that this place was much larger than she had previously thought.

“Here,” she gave Isabella the taser. “Do you know how to use that?”

Isabella nodded.

“Okay good. Hopefully you won’t have to, but you can use it to protect yourself,” Rio told her as they crossed the room.

She went to pull on the next door when…

Axe?

In the corner of the room was a bloody axe. It had clearly been used for some form of torture or execution. Maybe they were even planning on using it on her. Well, jokes on them. Now it was Rio’s.

She grinned as she darted across the room to grab it.

Isabella raised an eyebrow as she opened the door to let Rio through. Rio could only muster a shrug.

Now they were in another long corridor, and Noa was down the other end. The man carrying her had picked up his pace. He yelled at her to stop screaming, and there was a trail of Noa’s blood going down the length of the hallway.

That man was going to die.

“You might not want to see this,” Rio warned Isabella. “So, stay back.”

She sprinted towards Noa and the man, axe in hand. With no doors for them to escape through, Rio caught up to them easily.

Usually, she’d go for the most devastating play first. Maybe hack off a limb or a head. But he was holding Noa, and she didn’t want him to drop her.

Rio crashed to the ground, knees sliding until she could swipe at the man’s leg. A large cut appeared in his trousers as he grunted, leg buckling. Rio slid past him before getting to her feet and grabbing Noa before he could drop her.

She gave her to Isabella and said:

“Turn her away and cover her ears.”

As soon as Isabella did, Rio didn’t hesitate before she buried the axe in the man’s back. Blood sprayed, coating her body in it.

Fuck.

Rio didn’t mind blood, but she was currently trying to protect a child. She definitely should not be covered in human blood whilst doing so.

Fuck. Fuck. Fuck.

She tried to wipe it off before Noa noticed.

Too late.

“What are you doing?” Noa asked her.

When Rio looked up, blue eyes were glued to her.

“Erm…”

“I’ve seen blood before. I’ve actually seen worse. You don’t need to hide that from me.”

Rio stooped so that she was looking up at her. “Yes, but you were never supposed to see those things. I don’t want you to see anymore of it.”

Noa shrugged. “It’s too late for that.”

She was five, and yet she was talking like someone ten years older.

“You’re killing the people who hurt us, Rio. They’re bad people, and I know you’re a secret spy or something. That’s what they said. So, do it.”

Rio smiled. She still wasn’t going to kill anyone with Noa watching, but it was the fight in her. It, like a lot of things about Noa, reminded her of her wife.

“How’s your arm?” Rio asked.

“It hurts,” Noa replied.

Rio bit her lip. The cut was nasty and hadn’t stopped dripping.

“Okay. We’re gonna do this,” Rio told her as she got out her knife. She cut off the bottom of her top to act as a makeshift bandage and wrapped it around Noa’s arm.

“When you get out of here, Isa will find you a better one.”

“When we,” Noa corrected.

Rio nodded with a weak smile, although she knew she wasn’t going anywhere. Not with Nicky under threat.

Was Rio hearing things, or was that a gunshot? Was that two gunshots?

Clearly, she wasn’t, as Isabella and Noa looked around as if trying to find the source. Who would be-

Agatha.

Oh, yes. Her wife was here. Rio had almost forgotten in all the commotion.

Footsteps, a lot of them, had sounded in the next corridor over. They all seemed to be going in the direction of said gunshots, towards Agatha. And Rio being Rio, simply couldn’t let that happen.

“Stay here,” Rio told them before she ran down to the other end of the corridor.

She stepped out into the next hallway and all of the five men running towards her stopped. Their expressions were perplexed and sceptical and Rio wished she could read their minds. ‘How the hell has she gotten out?’ Was probably on their minds.

“We’re not supposed to kill her yet,” one of the men told his friends.

“Well, what are we supposed to do? She’s out?”

Rio rolled her eyes. She didn’t have time for this.

She ran towards the first man and swung. His head dropped to the ground. This time, the blood had splattered mostly on her face. The man had been a decent head taller than her (ha, get it?). The man just behind him gasped in horror as the man next to him brought a quivering hand holding a gun up. Before he could even think to shoot, Rio cut his hand off.

He screamed in agony before Rio buried her axe in his heart. More blood splattered her body. She went to free it before the next man along the line tackled her, slamming her against the wall. He had a syringe in his hand and was trying desperately to jam it into her arm.

He’d only been able to tackle her because of the element of surprise. Now, him trying to beat her in what was essentially an arm wrestle was just sad. She had no problem snapping his wrist before taking the syringe and shoving it into his arm instead.

She watched as his eyes began to get heavy.

“Night, night,” she told him as his body slumped to the ground.

Rio didn’t get the chance to breathe before another fist was flying in her direction. She dodged it easily, making the fist slam into the wall beside her head. The man yelped before she kneed him in the balls, freed her knife and stabbed him in the neck. A steady fountain of blood sprayed from it and onto her arm that was holding the knife in place.

She yanked it free and let the man’s body drop to the floor. Now with no more men flying at her, she could get her axe back. Rio counted the bodies as she stepped over them.

One, two, three, four…missing one.

The man with one hand was trying to escape.

I don’t fucking think so.

Rio ripped her axe from where it was buried in the man’s heart before throwing it hard and fast at the man running down the corridor. The axe spun multiple times before it hit home in the man’s back.

Rio nodded, satisfied with her work.

Once she’d gotten her axe back, she told Isabella and Noa to come out, and they headed down the other end of the corridor so they wouldn’t see the mess Rio had made.

There was no hiding the blood from Noa now, but it appeared the little girl genuinely didn’t care. She took Rio’s axeless hand and held it, blood and all.

***

This place really was a maze. Rio was unsure how many corridors they’d been down, but they never seemed to stop. They’d come across more herds of men, and just like last time, Rio would tell Isabella and Noa to stay in the corridor over, and she’d handle it.

Rio was certain she could fill multiple buckets with the amount of blood on her skin and clothes. She was starting to get worried that the sight might worry Noa, but it never did. Every time they would reunite, Noa would take her hand as if it were nothing.

Which, Rio figured, to her, it probably was.

She hated that the little girl had, had to grow up in an environment like this. And to make things worse, her parents were dead, and she didn’t even know.

When they came up to a door that actually looked like there was something promising behind it, Rio’s arms were dead. She’d lost count of how many people she’d killed.

Isabella pulled the large door open, and it revealed a massive space filled with nothing but the odd car.

Rio ushered the girls forward so that they were concealed behind a black Range Rover.

And then Rio saw her.

Her wife.

She was holding a woman by her hair and shoving her into the centre of the place. Agatha wouldn’t have been able to see her from where she was hidden to the left of her.

Agatha was covered in blood, which didn’t surprise Rio. She expected nothing less.

“Is that…is that your wife?” Isabella asked.

A smile spread across Rio’s lips. “Yep.”

She could feel Isabella's gaze over her before returning it to Agatha. “I can see why you two are married now.”

“She’s so cool!” Noa whisper yelled.

“Isn’t she?” Rio replied as if she were some fangirl talking about their favourite celebrity.

BANG!

A gunshot sounded and then another. Rio sheltered Noa with her body as she tried to find where the gun was firing from. She was unsuccessful.

There was a pause in fire before it started up again. This round shorter as her wife had found the target and killed them. Rio hadn’t seen a thing, but she knew.

“You fucking idiots!” Marina. How was she still speaking or even alive? Rio stabbed her in the fucking throat. “You’re not supposed to shoot her; I need her alive!”

And there it was again. The confirmation that they didn’t want her wife dead. Good. But why? They had no problem threatening a five-year-old boy, but drew the line at a thirty-three-year-old?

Rio poked her head out so she could see over the hood of the car and didn’t think before she grabbed her axe and bolted towards the horrific scene. A beefy man was holding Agatha up by the collar of her beautifully bloodied white shirt.

Men came at her from wherever they were hiding almost immediately. There were no thoughts behind Rio’s actions like she were working on autopilot. Just swing, swing kill. It reminded her of the wooden plank vs those protestors in Central Park when Agatha’s mother had trapped her.

It was like her mind was hardwired to protect Agatha without a thought, like it was animal instinct. That science couldn’t explain it. It was something Rio just did.

The men were dead, Rio was running forward, and Agatha had freed herself. The beefy man was hunched over on the floor a bit away, and her wife was sliding on the floor to retrieve something. She spun around, a bat raised and ready to crack Rio’s skull with.

She brought her axe up to prevent that from happening.

Her wife was the hottest woman on the planet.

Agatha’s smile mirrored hers, and Rio would’ve gotten lost in it if there hadn’t been a man gunning for her wife.

“Duck,” Rio told her.

Agatha didn’t need to be told twice. She ducked, and Rio cut the approaching man’s head off.

Her wife sprang back up. “The axe is hot, baby.”

And as if that was the first thing Agatha said to her after everything that had happened between them.

Rio couldn’t help it. She laughed. “Thank you. I like the bat.”

“Than-”

Her wife cut herself off when she pushed Rio down just before a knife connected with her body. The knife landed on the floor with a clatter before Agatha whacked someone in the head with her bat.

“Thank you. I feel like Harley Quinn.”

“Who –” Rio threw her pocket knife into the eye of the man coming up behind Agatha. “ – Who the fuck is Harley Quinn?”

“Are you fucking with me?” Agatha said as she nodded in the direction she wanted to head in. Rio followed her lead. “I know you didn’t watch films until you met me, but come on. You don’t know Harley Quinn?”

“Nope,” Rio replied as Agatha bent down to retrieve her gun and then the one just ahead of it.

“We’re watching it when we get home, then.” She handed the gun to Rio. “Now, as much as I’ve loved getting my hands dirty, let’s finish this with guns,” Agatha grinned.

Rio returned it.

“There will be no need for that,” a voice said.

There was absolutely no fucking way.

Wrinkled ankles revealed themselves as they got out of the car furthest away. Rio locked eyes with ice blue.

Because who else would it fucking be than Evanora Harkness.

Tina was a part of the Serpiente gang, she was also an FBI agent. An agent who had been asked to go to the home of a certain missing princess to retain her. After Agent Rio Vidal had leaked government secrets to her gang, she was a wanted criminal.

A missing wanted criminal.

She and her wife, Agent Agatha Harkness, last known location was the Serpiente’s headquarters. After a particular bloody blowout, the two women, along with Rio Vidal’s sister (the other missing heir), Agent’s Alice Wu-Gulliver, Jennifer Kale and Agent Agatha’s son had simply…

…Vanished.

The FBI had picked their best agents to go to the pair's house in hopes of finding them there.

Tina waited for her head agent to bash the door in before her task force swarmed the place.

When Tina stepped inside, the first thing she noticed was a ‘Happy Birthday’ banner in the hallway, written in gold a purple.

Ah, yes.

Tina remembered that the mysterious old woman who had planned the entire thing had asked for Rio Vidal to be kidnapped on Agatha Harkness’ birthday.

Tina ventured further in, her gun up, darting about the place as she followed the tail of five other agents. She stepped into the living room and found more banners, purple, white and gold balloons littered the floor and on the table, a handful of untouched and unopened presents.

Tina wondered if the FBI might let her take some.

Once the living room was confirmed to be clear, she moved to the kitchen. It was a lovely kitchen, open plan with oak furbishing. Rio Vidal and Agatha Harkness had a magnificent house, it was a shame they would have to live in prison cells for the foreseeable future.

Tina noticed a large paper bag that sat on the kitchen island next to two cups of coffee. She would recognise that branding anywhere.

Jo’s bagels.

Tina loved Jo’s bagels! She wondered how long the food had been sitting there. It was probably mouldy by now.

What sounded like boots on glass caught her attention, and she looked to see that one of the other agents had trodden on a piece of shattered glass. She walked over to it and saw blood.

She knew it was Vidal’s blood. Daniel hadn’t stopped boasting about how he’d caught her completely off guard the day he went to kidnap her.

A foul smell wafted up Tina’s nose, and she snapped her head up to lay eyes on a gone-off tray of tres leches. She wrinkled her nose and made quick work of vacating the kitchen.

She was ordered to go upstairs with five of her task team to sweep the top floor.

When the elevator opened, her team spread out. She went into the first bedroom and searched it, finding nothing to note other than the fact that this must have been Harkness’ son’s room. There were stuffed animals and Spider-Man posters stuck about the place.

Tina did feel bad about what her gang had threatened to do to the boy. He was only five, and this really had nothing to do with him. But like all people, he was a means to an end. She was sure they would’ve only killed him if it was necessary. It just so happened that the boy was the perfect leverage to keep Vidal in line.

Tina moved on to the next room, which was fitted with white bedsheets and purple and green cushions. Clothes were on the floor, as if someone had been changing in a rush. She went into the bathroom, and when she was certain no one was in it, she turned to leave.

That’s when Tina’s eyes snagged on a photo on the bedside table.

It was Vidal and her ‘mad wife’ as her gang members had labelled her. They appeared to be on holiday, Italy, if Tina had to guess. They were snuggled into a couch on the back of a yacht, champagne glasses in hand. They weren’t looking at the camera. They were looking at each other.

Tina thought they looked so in love. And they were.

She was there when Harkness was crashing out at the FBI headquarters when they couldn’t find Vidal (Tina had a hand in throwing them off the scent). She had heard what Vidal had done to her wife in order to protect her from Daniel when she was back with the Serpiente’s.

Tina thought that type of love was only written in movies. Tina had been proven wrong.

When she stepped out of this room, all the others, along with the rooftop garden, had been checked. They weren’t there.

The task team circled back to the first floor, and everyone confirmed what Tina had figured.

Rio Vidal and Agatha Harkness were gone.
